# CODEX RECOVERY AND INTEGRATION PROMPT

## User
**Timestamp:** 2026-07-19T00:16:19.418Z

CODEX RECOVERY AND INTEGRATION PROMPT

Consolidate Vision Waypoint Phases B-1 Through B-6 Into One Canonical Application

You are performing a complete recovery, audit, reconciliation, and integration of the Vision Waypoint Phase B implementation.

The implementation appears to have been developed across multiple separate Git worktrees or cloned working directories:

Codex_TreasureHunt
Codex_TreasureHunt-phaseb2
Codex_TreasureHunt-phaseb3
Codex_TreasureHunt-phaseb4
Codex_TreasureHunt-phaseb5
Codex_TreasureHunt-phaseb6

These phase directories were intended to support parallel work, not to become permanently separate applications.

The final required result is:

One canonical repository
One integrated codebase
One coherent database migration history
One shared set of domain contracts
One shared Player interface
One shared Captain interface
One shared Studio interface
One canonical development server
One canonical port: 3000

Do not blindly copy files from one phase directory into another.

Do not assume that a Codex chat reporting completion means its work was merged.

Do not assume GitHub main contains all completed Phase B work.

Do not delete any worktree, clone, folder, branch, commit, migration, untracked file, or local change until the complete recovery and integration has been reviewed.

⸻

1. Primary Mission

Recover and integrate all legitimate work from Vision Waypoint Phases B-1 through B-6 into one canonical integration branch.

You must:

1. Identify the exact repository/worktree arrangement.
2. Preserve every phase implementation.
3. Determine what each phase actually completed.
4. Identify all branches, commits, uncommitted changes, and generated artifacts.
5. Compare each phase against its original governing prompt.
6. Reconcile overlapping source changes.
7. Consolidate database migrations.
8. Consolidate domain and protocol contracts.
9. Port phase functionality into the current canonical UI.
10. Run focused validation after each phase is integrated.
11. Run complete validation after all phases are combined.
12. Publish the integration branch safely.
13. Produce a detailed integration and recovery report.
14. Stop for review before merging into main.
15. Preserve all phase worktrees until final approval.

This is both:

* a repository recovery task;
* and a full software integration task.

It is not merely a Git merge exercise.

⸻

2. Governing Source-of-Truth Order

Before modifying source, locate and read all applicable governing material.

The governing order is:

1. TT-VISION-GOV-001
   Vision Waypoint and External AR Governing Specification
2. TT-VISION-PHASE-B-001
   Phase B Implementation Roadmap
3. Original prompts for Phases B-1 through B-6
4. Phase-specific ADRs and implementation records
5. Existing project-wide architecture and design documentation
6. Current canonical repository conventions
7. This recovery and integration prompt

Expected locations may include:

Development_Docs/
Development_Docs/AR/
Development_Docs/AR/ADRs/
Development_Docs/AR/Phase_B1/
Development_Docs/AR/Phase_B2/
Development_Docs/AR/Phase_B3/
Development_Docs/AR/Phase_B4/
Development_Docs/AR/Phase_B5/
Development_Docs/AR/Phase_B6/
Codex_Chats/

Search thoroughly.

Do not invent replacement architecture merely because phase implementations disagree.

When two implementations conflict, use the governing documents and semantic dependency order to determine the correct combined design.

Record any material decision in an ADR or integration decision log.

⸻

3. Non-Negotiable Safety Rules

Before changing anything:

1. Identify the canonical repository path.
2. Identify every Codex_TreasureHunt-phaseb* directory.
3. Determine whether each directory is:
    * a linked Git worktree;
    * a separate full clone;
    * a copied folder;
    * a detached worktree;
    * a generated build output;
    * or another arrangement.
4. Record the exact state of every directory.
5. Preserve all staged changes.
6. Preserve all unstaged changes.
7. Preserve all untracked files.
8. Preserve all local branches.
9. Preserve all stashes.
10. Preserve all phase-specific commits.
11. Preserve all migration files.
12. Preserve all phase documentation and completion reports.

Never use:

git reset --hard
git clean
git checkout -- .
git restore .
git restore --staged .
git stash --all
force push
broad file-copy replacement
automatic conflict resolution using only ours
automatic conflict resolution using only theirs

Do not delete or remove any worktree.

Do not run cleanup tools against the phase folders.

Do not allow generated dependency folders such as node_modules, .next, build output, caches, or temporary databases to influence source integration.

Do not stage unrelated files using broad commands such as:

git add .
git add -A

Stage intentionally by path.

⸻

4. Canonical Recovery Branch

Perform the recovery from the canonical Codex_TreasureHunt repository.

Create a dedicated integration branch, for example:

integration/vision-waypoint-b1-b6

The integration branch must be based on the correct current canonical branch.

Before creating it, record:

* canonical branch;
* canonical HEAD;
* upstream;
* ahead/behind status;
* remote HEAD;
* worktree status;
* untracked files;
* active development server;
* current database configuration;
* current port usage.

Do not modify main directly.

Do not merge the integration branch into main automatically.

Push the integration branch after successful checkpoints and final validation.

⸻

5. Complete Worktree and Clone Inventory

From the canonical repository, run and record:

git worktree list --porcelain
git branch --all --verbose
git log --all --graph --decorate --oneline
git remote -v
git status --short --branch
git stash list

Inside every Phase B directory, run:

git rev-parse --show-toplevel
git rev-parse --git-common-dir
git rev-parse --git-dir
git branch --show-current
git rev-parse HEAD
git rev-parse --abbrev-ref --symbolic-full-name @{upstream}
git status --short --branch
git remote -v
git stash list
git log --oneline --decorate --max-count=30
git merge-base HEAD main

If an upstream does not exist, record that fact without treating it as failure.

For every directory, record:

Absolute path
Repository identity
Worktree or clone
Branch
HEAD commit
Base commit
Remote
Upstream
Ahead/behind state
Staged files
Unstaged files
Untracked files
Stashes
Relevant commits
Build artifacts
Database files
Environment files
Last modified time

Create:

Development_Docs/AR/Phase_B_Integration/
  Phase_B_Worktree_Inventory.md

⸻

6. Preserve Uncommitted Phase Work

If any phase folder contains uncommitted source changes:

1. Inspect every changed file.
2. Separate source from generated output.
3. Do not commit:
    * node_modules;
    * .next;
    * build output;
    * logs;
    * temporary database copies;
    * local secrets;
    * caches.
4. Create a preservation branch specific to that phase if needed.
5. Commit legitimate uncommitted source with a clearly labeled recovery commit.

Example:

recovery/phase-b4-uncommitted

Example commit:

recovery(vision): preserve uncommitted phase B-4 work

Do not alter the intent of the work during preservation.

The initial goal is to ensure that no source exists only as an uncommitted local file.

⸻

7. Recover Separate Clone History

If any phase directory is a separate clone rather than a shared worktree:

1. Verify that it points to the same repository origin.
2. Identify its unique branch and commits.
3. Add it temporarily as a local recovery remote if necessary.
4. Fetch the relevant branch and commit history into the canonical repository.
5. Preserve exact commit identities where practical.
6. Do not push unrelated local branches.
7. Do not overwrite an existing branch with a different history.

Example temporary remote names:

phaseb2-recovery
phaseb3-recovery
phaseb4-recovery
phaseb5-recovery
phaseb6-recovery

After fetching, verify that every unique source commit can be addressed from the canonical repository.

Document the recovery method.

⸻

8. Phase Provenance and Completeness Audit

Create a full provenance matrix for B-1 through B-6.

For each phase, identify:

* original prompt;
* governing requirements;
* source folder;
* source branch;
* starting commit;
* ending commit;
* merge base;
* unique commit range;
* changed source files;
* deleted files;
* migration files;
* schema changes;
* dependencies added;
* environment variables added;
* API routes added;
* domain types added;
* protocol types added;
* frontend components added;
* native/desktop files added;
* PWA files added;
* tests added;
* documentation added;
* implementation record;
* completion report;
* test results claimed;
* test results reproducible;
* uncommitted work;
* pushed state;
* merged state;
* conflicts with other phases;
* stale-base risks;
* placeholder or mock status;
* actual completion percentage.

Create:

Development_Docs/AR/Phase_B_Integration/
  Phase_B1_B6_Provenance_Matrix.md
  Phase_B1_B6_Changed_Files.csv
  Phase_B1_B6_Test_Evidence.md
  Phase_B1_B6_Completion_Assessment.md

Do not classify a phase as complete based only on:

* chat completion;
* documentation;
* scaffolding;
* placeholder interfaces;
* a passing typecheck;
* mock-only behavior where production behavior was required;
* isolated build success.

Use source and test evidence.

⸻

9. Dependency Analysis

Determine the actual logical dependencies among B-1 through B-6.

The default expectation is:

B-1
Shared platform, domain, versioning, protocol, adapters
B-2
Capture companion and acquisition infrastructure
B-3
Vision build, package, inference, and verification pipeline
B-4
Studio authoring, reference collection, calibration, testing
B-5
Player and Captain runtime integration
B-6
Production hardening, rollout, observability, certification

Do not assume all phases were implemented from the output of the prior phase.

Check each phase’s merge base.

If B-3, B-4, B-5, or B-6 were all created directly from B-1, integration must explicitly combine their independent changes.

Create:

Development_Docs/AR/Phase_B_Integration/
  Phase_B_Dependency_Graph.md

Identify:

* hard dependencies;
* soft dependencies;
* overlapping files;
* overlapping migrations;
* overlapping contracts;
* ordering constraints;
* required adaptation work.

⸻

10. Integration Plan Before Code Changes

Before merging or cherry-picking any implementation commit, create:

Development_Docs/AR/Phase_B_Integration/
  Phase_B1_B6_Integration_Plan.md

The plan must define:

1. Integration order.
2. Branches or commit ranges to incorporate.
3. Commits to exclude.
4. Reasons for exclusions.
5. Shared files likely to conflict.
6. Database migration strategy.
7. Contract consolidation strategy.
8. UI adaptation strategy.
9. Test sequence.
10. Rollback checkpoints.
11. Validation ownership.
12. Port and server isolation.
13. Database isolation.
14. Final publication plan.

Do not begin broad integration until this plan exists.

⸻

11. Commit Selection Rules

For each phase, classify commits into:

APPLICATION_SOURCE
DATABASE_MIGRATION
TESTS
DOCUMENTATION
CHAT_SYNC
GENERATED_OUTPUT
ENVIRONMENT_ONLY
RECOVERY
UNRELATED

Integrate:

* application source;
* legitimate migrations;
* tests;
* relevant documentation;
* relevant recovery commits.

Usually exclude or separately handle:

* chat synchronization commits;
* generated build artifacts;
* local environment files;
* dependency caches;
* unrelated product work;
* duplicate documentation synchronization.

Do not cherry-pick chat-sync commits merely because they are adjacent to application commits.

Do not lose phase implementation work hidden inside mixed commits. If a mixed commit contains both application source and unrelated changes, extract the relevant patch carefully and document it.

⸻

12. Controlled Phase Integration

Integrate each phase in the dependency order determined by the roadmap and audit.

The expected checkpoint sequence is:

integration(vision): incorporate phase B-1 foundation
integration(vision): incorporate phase B-2 capture infrastructure
integration(vision): incorporate phase B-3 vision pipeline
integration(vision): incorporate phase B-4 studio tooling
integration(vision): incorporate phase B-5 runtime experience
integration(vision): incorporate phase B-6 hardening

After each phase:

1. Resolve conflicts semantically.
2. Run formatting on changed files.
3. Run focused typecheck.
4. Run focused unit tests.
5. Run focused schema tests.
6. Run focused integration tests.
7. Record failures and fixes.
8. Create a checkpoint commit.
9. Push the integration branch.
10. Continue only when the current checkpoint is coherent.

Do not wait until all phases are merged before discovering that B-2 broke B-1’s contracts.

⸻

13. Conflict Resolution Rules

Never resolve a conflict using blanket “ours” or “theirs.”

For each conflict:

1. Identify which phase introduced each side.
2. Identify the governing requirement.
3. Identify newer canonical improvements on main.
4. Determine whether both sides contain valid behavior.
5. Build the combined implementation.
6. Add or update tests proving the resolution.
7. Record the decision.

Maintain:

Development_Docs/AR/Phase_B_Integration/
  Phase_B_Conflict_Resolution_Log.md

For every conflict record:

File
Phases involved
Original intent
Conflict cause
Chosen behavior
Code retained from each side
Tests added
Remaining limitation

⸻

14. Protect Current Canonical UI Work

The current canonical branch may contain newer:

* navigation;
* unified shell;
* color system;
* responsive behavior;
* Tall Tale journal UI;
* accessibility improvements;
* animation changes;
* Player Library changes;
* Captain Library changes;
* Studio changes.

Do not restore stale phase-specific UI wholesale.

Where a phase branch contains functionality but older presentation code:

1. Extract the functional behavior.
2. Port it into the current canonical component structure.
3. Use the current design system.
4. Preserve current navigation.
5. Preserve current color/theme behavior.
6. Preserve current responsive layout.
7. Preserve current accessibility behavior.
8. Preserve canonical journal usage.

The final product must not feel like six different applications taped together at the edges.

⸻

15. Shared Contract Consolidation

Create one authoritative implementation for each shared contract.

Explicitly audit and reconcile:

* VisionWaypoint;
* VisionWaypointVersion;

* verification profiles;
* sharing scopes;

* story waypoint binding;

* Captain decision;
* progression event;
* feature flags;
* capability detection;
* platform adapters;
* desktop bridge;
* PWA bridge;
* protocol errors;
* telemetry;
* audit records.

There must not be phase-local duplicate versions of these contracts after integration.

Use schema validation at trust boundaries.

Preserve backwards compatibility where required.

Document any schema version bump.

⸻

16. Database and Migration Reconciliation

Database integration must remain serialized.

Create:

Development_Docs/AR/Phase_B_Integration/
  Phase_B_Migration_Ledger.md

For every migration record:

* phase;
* filename;
* parent schema state;
* models added;
* fields added;
* fields changed;
* indexes;
* unique constraints;
* foreign keys;
* data migrations;
* rollback implications;
* whether it was applied anywhere;
* conflict with another phase.

Identify whether phases created migrations independently from the same schema baseline.

Do not simply sort conflicting migrations by timestamp.

The final migration history must support:

1. Clean database bootstrap.
2. Upgrade from the canonical pre-B schema.
3. Upgrade from B-1-only schema.
4. Seeded development database.
5. Test database creation.
6. ORM client generation.
7. Rollback or recovery documentation.

Preserve published-version immutability.

Preserve idempotency constraints.

Preserve exact-once story progression.

Preserve referential integrity.

If necessary, create a new integration migration that reconciles independent phase changes.

Do not edit already-applied production migrations unless absolutely necessary and documented.

⸻

17. Exactly-Once and Concurrency Verification

The combined system must prove:

* repeated verification submissions do not create duplicate accepted events;
* repeated processing does not advance the story twice;
* reused idempotency keys with altered payloads are rejected;
* stale verification results cannot advance a later story block;
* Captain fallback cannot double-complete an objective;
* automatic verification and Captain confirmation cannot both advance the story;
* retries are distinguishable from duplicates;
* session concurrency is enforced;
* publication cannot mutate an existing published waypoint version.

Use database transactions for multi-step state changes.

Unique constraints alone are not sufficient proof.

⸻

18. Front-End Integration Requirements

The final integrated application must use one shared frontend.

Studio

Integrate:

* waypoint library;
* create waypoint;
* edit draft;
* version history;
* reference collection;
* build status;
* calibration;
* test workflow;
* publication;
* immutable-version display;
* story binding;
* compatibility status;
* error recovery.

Player

Integrate:

* waypoint objective;
* Inspect Surroundings;
* permission state;
* capture state;
* verification progress;
* matched;
* not matched;
* low confidence;
* retry;
* timeout;
* offline;
* unavailable capability;
* Captain fallback;
* accessible status announcements;
* deterministic final story state.

Captain

Integrate:

* active verification requests;
* attempt history;
* safe evidence summary;
* accept;
* reject;
* request retry;
* fallback resolution;
* audit history;
* stale-request behavior.

Shared

Preserve:

* canonical navigation;
* current design system;
* current theme;
* responsive behavior;
* accessibility;
* motion preferences;
* role boundaries;
* Player-safe data projection.

⸻

19. Desktop and PWA Consolidation

The final system must not contain separate duplicated applications for:

* browser;
* PWA;
* Windows desktop.

The shared frontend must remain canonical.

Platform differences must exist behind adapters.

Audit:

* PWA manifest;
* service worker;
* cache boundaries;
* offline behavior;
* desktop shell;
* desktop bridge;
* capability detection;
* capture adapter;
* filesystem adapter;
* update behavior;
* protocol pairing;
* local service communication.

Do not cache private mutable API responses.

Do not store secrets in desktop source.

Do not permit silent capture.

Do not create a second desktop-only story engine.

⸻

20. Feature Flag Consolidation

Create one authoritative feature-flag system.

At minimum reconcile:

visionWaypoints.enabled
visionWaypoints.studio.enabled
visionWaypoints.player.enabled
visionWaypoints.mockVerifier.enabled
visionWaypoints.capture.enabled
visionWaypoints.buildPipeline.enabled
visionWaypoints.externalProvider.enabled
visionWaypoints.captainFallback.enabled
visionWaypoints.pwa.enabled
visionWaypoints.desktop.enabled

Feature flags and runtime capabilities must remain separate.

The UI must resolve:

feature enabled
platform supported
permission available
provider available
package compatible
offline capable
fallback available

Do not expose controls that cannot function.

⸻

21. Security and Privacy Review

Perform a focused security review covering:

* raw frame handling;
* screenshot handling;
* evidence retention;
* pairing tokens;
* provider authentication;
* request replay;
* session binding;
* waypoint-version binding;
* package hash validation;
* unsupported schema versions;
* unsafe external input;
* API authorization;
* Captain permissions;
* Studio publication permissions;
* local desktop bridge exposure;
* service-worker caching;
* logging of private story data.

Do not store raw image data in generic JSON fields.

Do not expose unpublished waypoint data to Players.

Do not allow a provider result to claim Captain authority.

Do not silently capture frames.

Record findings in:

Development_Docs/AR/Phase_B_Integration/
  Phase_B_Security_Privacy_Review.md

⸻

22. Test and Validation Environment Isolation

Before mutating tests:

1. Identify the canonical database.
2. Create a unique isolated test database or copy.
3. Use an explicit absolute database connection.
4. Record the database identity.
5. Record the development server PID.
6. Record the validation port.
7. Verify the application is connected to the isolated database.
8. Preserve the canonical database hash, size, and modification time.
9. Run mutations only against the isolated test database.
10. Verify the canonical database remains unchanged.

Do not run integration tests against a shared local development database.

Do not use port 3000 for temporary validation if the existing canonical server already owns it.

Temporary isolated ports are allowed during integration.

The final canonical application must run on port 3000.

⸻

23. Required Focused Tests

After integrating each phase, run the relevant focused tests.

The final integrated suite must include:

Domain

* waypoint creation;
* draft version creation;
* immutable publication;
* new draft from published version;
* lifecycle transition validation;
* compatibility validation;
* story binding to exact version.

Protocol

* valid request;
* invalid schema;
* unsupported schema;
* wrong waypoint version;
* wrong package hash;
* wrong session;
* expired request;
* duplicate event;
* altered duplicate payload;
* invalid confidence;
* invalid provider authority.

Story engine

* successful verification completes once;
* failed verification does not complete;
* retry succeeds;
* duplicate success does not duplicate progression;
* stale success does not progress;
* Captain confirmation completes once;
* automatic and Captain paths cannot both complete;
* refresh does not repeat completion.

Studio

* create;
* edit;
* publish;
* clone version;
* bind;
* preview;
* calibration failure;
* incompatible package;
* validation errors.

Player

* ready;
* requesting;
* capturing;
* verifying;
* success;
* failure;
* retry;
* timeout;
* offline;
* unsupported;
* Captain fallback;
* keyboard;
* screen reader;
* reduced motion.

Captain

* request list;
* detail;
* approve;
* reject;
* retry request;
* stale request;
* duplicate decision;
* audit history.

PWA and desktop

* capability resolution;
* adapter selection;
* unsupported fallback;
* offline shell;
* safe caching;
* desktop bridge validation;
* no duplicate frontend implementation.

⸻

24. Required End-to-End Proof

Run a complete isolated end-to-end workflow:

Studio creates waypoint
        ↓
Draft version is persisted
        ↓
Reference data is attached or mocked as allowed
        ↓
Build/test process runs
        ↓
Immutable version is published
        ↓
Story block binds exact published version
        ↓
Story is published
        ↓
Playthrough starts
        ↓
Player reaches waypoint objective
        ↓
Inspect Surroundings is invoked
        ↓
Correct platform adapter runs
        ↓
Verification request is persisted
        ↓
Verification result is validated
        ↓
Story advances exactly once
        ↓
Browser refresh occurs
        ↓
Story remains advanced once
        ↓
Duplicate result is submitted
        ↓
No duplicate progression occurs

Also prove:

Failure
Retry
Timeout
Stale result
Captain confirmation
Unsupported capability
Offline behavior
Package incompatibility

Record exact requests, events, database rows, and terminal states without exposing secrets.

⸻

25. Runtime and Port Consolidation

At the end of integration:

* one canonical source tree must contain all Phase B functionality;
* one canonical development command must start the app;
* one canonical environment must be documented;
* one canonical database configuration must be used;
* one canonical development server must run on port 3000.

Do not leave phase-specific builds presented as separate product versions.

Phase worktrees may remain for safety, but they must not be required to run the application.

Document which old ports were used temporarily and confirm they are not part of the final workflow.

⸻

26. Final Repository Validation

Run repository-supported commands, including appropriate equivalents of:

npm run format:check
npm run lint
npm run typecheck
npm test
npm run assets:validate
npm run build
npm run validate

Also run:

* database migration validation;
* clean bootstrap;
* seeded bootstrap;
* protocol compatibility tests;
* focused Phase B E2E;
* PWA build validation;
* desktop build validation where supported.

Do not run multiple full validation suites concurrently against the same build directory or database.

Classify every result as:

PASS
FAIL
SKIPPED
BLOCKED
ENVIRONMENTAL
BASELINE FAILURE
TASK REGRESSION

A skipped test is not a pass.

⸻

* commands;

Final state

* canonical start command;
* canonical server port;

* worktrees preserved;

⸻

28. GitHub Publication

Push the integration branch to GitHub.

Open a draft pull request targeting main.

The draft PR must include:

* phase provenance summary;
* integration sequence;
* migration notes;
* conflict summary;
* validation summary;
* known limitations;
* worktrees preserved;
* explicit statement that the PR is not yet merged.

Do not merge the PR automatically.

Do not delete source branches automatically.

Do not remove worktrees automatically.

Stop for human review after the integration branch and report are complete.

⸻

29. Completion Gate

Do not declare this task complete unless all of the following are true:

1. Every phase directory has been inventoried.
2. Every phase branch and commit is accounted for.
3. Every uncommitted source change has been preserved.
4. Every phase has been assessed against its original prompt.
5. All valid Phase B source exists in one integration branch.
6. No entire phase folder was copied blindly over another.
7. Shared contracts have one authoritative implementation.
8. Database migrations form one valid sequence.
9. Published waypoint versions remain immutable.
10. Story progression remains exactly-once.
11. Stale results cannot progress the story.
12. Player, Captain, and Studio use one shared application.
13. Browser, PWA, and desktop use shared frontend source.
14. The current canonical UI and navigation are preserved.
15. Focused tests pass or failures are documented.
16. Full validation passes or blockers are documented.
17. The integrated application runs from the canonical repository.
18. The canonical application runs on port 3000.
19. The integration branch is pushed.
20. A draft PR is created.
21. The final report is complete.
22. Old phase folders and worktrees remain preserved.

Final verification\n\nBefore claiming completion:\n\n- re-read the original user request and governing sources;\n- map every acceptance criterion to a delivered change or verified result;\n- reconcile every lane output and resolve or disclose contradictions;\n- confirm no material agent result remains unreviewed;\n- inspect the complete integrated diff and working tree for accidental scope expansion;\n- verify shared-file ownership and handoffs are complete;\n- run required focused, integrated, runtime, regression, accessibility, performance, security, migration, build, or acceptance checks as applicable;\n- distinguish skipped, unverified, pre-existing, and failed checks;\n- confirm generated artifacts and unrelated work were not accidentally staged or treated as source; and\n- run the single coordinator-owned repository finalization gate from `AGENTS.md`.\n\nFor documentation-only work, use proportionate document validation and do not launch the application or full test suite unless a governing instruction explicitly requires it.\n\n### 24. Final report format\n\nThe coordinator reports:\n\n```text\nOutcome: what was completed\nParallel execution: lanes, modes, ownership boundaries, waves, maximum concurrency, and why the decomposition was safe/useful\nSubagent lifecycle: total unique workers; important results; failed, blocked, replaced, or cancelled lanes; and reconciliation/integration status\nParallel execution outcome for substantial tasks: effect on throughput, capacity, depth/coverage, verification, elapsed time, duplication/overhead, and improvements for the next decomposition\nAffected files/systems: task-authored changes, sync-owned changes, and pre-existing work classified separately\nValidation: commands/checks, exit status, and material evidence\nFailures/limitations: unresolved or skipped checks and why\nRemaining risks: known risks that remain within or outside scope\nFollow-up: only work genuinely outside the requested scope\nChat archive: required synchronization result\nDevelopment docs: required synchronization result\n```\n\nFor every substantial task that used subagents, include the complete final parallel-execution summary required by the communication plan: total unique subagents, maximum simultaneous workers, waves, roles and ownership boundaries, read-only and write-enabled lanes, important results from each lane, failures/blocks/replacements/cancellations, reconciliation, realized capacity/depth/coverage/verification/time benefits, avoidable duplication or overhead, and decomposition improvements. Keep the assessment concise and evidence-based. Do not claim speculative numerical percentages unless timing or work data was actually recorded.\n\nFor every substantial task, the final execution assessment must also state concisely and from observed task evidence:\n\n- whether independent work began promptly;\n- whether useful capacity remained unnecessarily idle;\n- whether critical-path work received priority;\n- whether completed results were reviewed and integrated promptly;\n- whether parallelization materially reduced elapsed time;\n- what avoidable waiting, duplication, or planning overhead occurred; and\n- how a similar future task could finish faster.\n\nDo not invent timing figures, duration estimates, or percentages that were not measured.\n\nThe report provides concise rationale, evidence, decisions, and results. It does not expose private chain-of-thought or paste raw agent logs.\n\n## Standard parallel workflow patterns\n\nAdapt these patterns to the task rather than copying them mechanically.\n\n### Repository-wide audit\n\nTypical lanes include repository/architecture census, one or more subsystem reviews, runtime behavior, performance, accessibility, security, testing, data integrity, documentation consistency, missing opportunities, evidence verification, and final reconciliation. Target six to twelve workers when that many real categories exist. Preserve the audit prompt, taxonomy, severity definitions, evidence rules, and report format; give each lane a bounded evidence surface; verify severe/disputed findings; and centralize deduplication, severity reconciliation, and the final coherent audit.\n\n### Multi-feature implementation\n\n1. Establish shared architecture/contracts and identify shared files.\n2. Place genuinely independent feature lanes in separate worktrees or assign disjoint paths.\n3. Give shared architecture, schemas, configuration, manifests, and lockfiles one owner.\n4. Let each feature lane run focused tests.\n5. Integrate in dependency order under one owner.\n6. Run final full-system verification once on the combined state.\n\n### Bug investigation\n\nPotential lanes include independent reproduction, static code tracing, runtime tracing, regression history, test-gap analysis, platform-specific behavior, dependency behavior, and alternative-hypothesis verification. Keep hypotheses distinct and evidence-backed. The coordinator reconciles them and selects a supported root cause before authorizing implementation. Parallel fixes for the same suspected defect are normally redundant unless intentionally comparing isolated approaches.\n\n### Refactor\n\nStart architecture mapping, consumer inventory, and test-baseline lanes in parallel. Serialize shared-interface changes under one owner, then fan out independent package/component migrations with disjoint ownership. Integrate in dependency order and run compatibility/regression verification after all consumers move.\n\n### Frontend experience work\n\nPotential lanes include route/shell structure, navigation, bounded component groups, animation/interaction, design-system consistency, responsive behavior, accessibility, performance, browser reproduction, test coverage, visual verification, and integration review. Use up to twelve when these are genuinely independent. Assign one owner to root layout, providers, shared tokens/global styles, and route shells, plus one runtime/browser owner. Finish with an integrated responsive, keyboard, motion-mode, console, performance, and UX review against the original acceptance criteria.\n\n### Backend or database work\n\nPotential lanes include API, services, repositories, schema analysis, data integrity, security, tests, operational readiness, observability, and documentation. Separate them only where evidence or files do not overlap. Give schemas and the ordered migration chain one authoritative writer and one database/migration operator. Serialize migration generation/application and shared state mutation. Integrate API/service contracts before final database, security, regression, and deployment-readiness validation.\n\n### Documentation task\n\nPotential lanes include source inventory, contradiction review, terminology, factual verification, structural review, instruction-discovery validation, configuration validation, and editorial integration. Fan out read-only discovery and fact-checking by topic. Topic-specific drafting may run in parallel only with disjoint document ownership. Use one editorial integration owner for shared documents, terminology, links, and final formatting. Verify claims against sources and run proportionate diff/format/link checks. Do not create extra helper documents when the requested output is fixed.\n\n### Homogeneous batch investigations\n\nWhen the installed client exposes `spawn_agents_on_csv` or a verified equivalent, optional batch fan-out may handle many independent items with the same analysis: one component, route, package, animation system, test failure, migration target, document, or incident per row. Treat this capability as client-surface dependent and experimental; use ordinary named lanes when clearer.\n\nEach batch requires a stable item ID, explicit input columns, fixed output schema, scope and non-scope, evidence fields, confidence, exactly one result per worker, bounded runtime, maximum safe concurrency, consolidated output, coordinator reconciliation, and retained error rows. Never silently drop failures or assume a batch tool exists without verifying the current client.\n\n## Anti-patterns\n\nDo not:\n\n- process independent areas sequentially without a concrete reason;\n- leave useful worker slots idle while ready meaningful work exists;\n- wait for an entire worker wave when one slot becomes available;\n- wait for every discovery lane before starting implementation that has sufficient verified inputs;\n- wait for every implementation lane before integrating completed independent work when incremental integration is safe;\n- require every worker to finish before reviewing completed high-priority output;\n- spawn agents with substantially identical scopes;\n- make every agent scan the entire repository;\n- make every worker rediscover repository structure instead of reusing a shared census;\n- delay safe read-only fan-out until every planning field is complete;\n- write oversized plans or status reports whose coordination cost exceeds their practical value;\n- perform delegable work in the coordinator merely because delegation requires a briefing;\n- launch work before evidence, path, and resource ownership are defined;\n- launch a write-enabled worker against an unresolved, inferred, shorthand, or otherwise unverified path;\n- treat a nonexistent path as writable without explicitly confirming and labeling intentional new-file ownership;\n- allow multiple agents to edit the same file concurrently;\n- let multiple development servers compete for port `3000`;\n- make every lane run the entire test suite;\n- rerun expensive global checks after every small lane instead of using focused checks and one integrated gate;\n- use agent count as a quality metric or create microscopic artificial lanes;\n- maintain redundant lanes after sufficient evidence exists;\n- ignore slower-lane results because faster lanes finished first;\n- combine reports without reconciling duplicates, severity, or contradictions;\n- let subagents reinterpret or broaden user requirements;\n- use parallelism to bypass safety, review, authorization, or validation;\n- restart completed work after one lane fails;\n- claim completion before integration and verification;\n- create alternate application copies, port-specific versions, or abandoned variants;\n- use generated snapshots or obsolete/source-history trees because they are easier to discover;\n- hide uncertainty, partial failure, skipped validation, or incomplete integration;\n- let workers independently fetch/rebase/merge/commit/push or run chat/document synchronization without explicit exclusive ownership; or\n- stage the whole repository by default in a dirty worktree.\n\n## Adaptive plan behavior\n\nUpdate the plan when:\n\n- new dependencies or shared resources are discovered;\n- two lanes overlap or shared-file conflict becomes likely;\n- a lane becomes unnecessary or duplicates another;\n- supposedly independent work is found to be dependent;\n- a blocked lane can be narrowed or split;\n- a slow or broad lane can be split or reassigned to shorten the critical path without losing useful work;\n- additional safe parallelism becomes available;\n- runtime evidence contradicts static analysis;\n- the canonical implementation differs from the initial assumption;\n- a write-lane path is verified, found nonexistent, confirmed as an intentional new file, or remains unresolved;\n- validation reveals a pre-existing failure or regression; or\n- risk, completion criteria, or user authority changes.\n\nWhen adapting:\n\n1. preserve completed work and useful partial evidence;\n2. update dependency edges, ownership, locks, status, risk, and validation;\n3. notify affected lanes and stop conflicting writers before reassignment;\n4. record the material discovery or decision;\n5. start newly ready independent work promptly;\n6. review and integrate completed high-priority output without waiting for unrelated lanes; and\n7. avoid unnecessary restarts.\n\nThe plan serves the task. It may evolve, but it may never override the user's instructions or governing product requirements. Codex must move as quickly as possible without becoming careless: progressive planning, specialization, early risk resolution, incremental integration, focused validation, and prompt worker reuse exist to deliver a correct and complete result in the least practical elapsed time.\n\r\n\r\n> C:\\Users\\kkids\\.codex\\memories\\MEMORY.md:1:# Task Group: TreasureHunt Vision Waypoint Phase B-6 release hardening \r\nand release-gate evidence\r\n> C:\\Users\\kkids\\.codex\\memories\\MEMORY.md:2:scope: Use for the isolated Vision Waypoint B-6 worktree, Windows \r\npackaging, development-installer provenance, release authority, and distinguishing local validation from \r\npublic/stable-release approval.\r\n  C:\\Users\\kkids\\.codex\\memories\\MEMORY.md:3:applies_to: cwd=C:\\Users\\kkids\\Documents\\Codex_TreasureHunt_Phase_B6; \r\nreuse_rule=checkout- and evidence-specific: revalidate the branch/remote SHA, current blockers, signing state, \r\ninstaller hash, and real-world evidence before using any release conclusion\r\n  C:\\Users\\kkids\\.codex\\memories\\MEMORY.md:4:\r\n  C:\\Users\\kkids\\.codex\\memories\\MEMORY.md:5:## Task 1: Implement and validate Phase B-6 release hardening, outcome \r\npartial\r\n  C:\\Users\\kkids\\.codex\\memories\\MEMORY.md:6:\r\n  C:\\Users\\kkids\\.codex\\memories\\MEMORY.md:7:### rollout_summary_files\r\n\r\n\r\n", "type": "input_text"}]

and\r\n- preserve completed work when the plan changes.\r\n\r\n## Capacity and wave scheduling\r\n\r\nRecord:\r\n\r\n```text\r\nConfigured open-thread capacity:\r\nCoordinator reservation:\r\nMaximum normal direct workers:\r\nCurrent ready lanes:\r\nCurrently active lanes:\r\nBlocked lanes:\r\nAvailable slots:\r\nNext ready lanes:\r\nHighest-value ready-lane queue:\r\nExclusive resources currently held:\r\n```\r\n\r\nKeep safe capacity filled with the highest-value ready meaningful work, reserve the coordinator when the client counts the root session, and maintain ready and next-ready queues for substantial tasks. Fill each newly available slot immediately rather than waiting for an entire wave. Capacity may remain intentionally unused only when no useful independent work exists or a concrete conflict, dependency, safety, or resource constraint prevents more work. When substantial ready work exists but a slot remains unused, record the reason briefly.\r\n\r\nDo not require a fixed worker count when fewer meaningful lanes exist, and do not create a lane merely because capacity is available. When enough real non-overlapping work exists, use the full safe and useful lane count. Avoid idle or artificial workers, stop or collapse redundant work after sufficient evidence exists, preserve results between waves, and keep completed high-priority output moving into review and integration.\r\n\r\n## Worker capability and reasoning-speed planning\r\n\r\nRoute work for both reliability and elapsed time. Use the fastest capable available worker configuration for mechanical inventories, repository searches, classifications, repetitive comparisons, and bounded read-only scans. Reserve high reasoning effort for work that actually needs it, and use stronger workers for difficult architecture, diagnosis, implementation, reconciliation, and verification. Do not assign maximum reasoning effort to every worker by habit.\r\n\r\nRecord any capability or reasoning requirement that materially affects lane success or urgency. Reassign work from an unnecessarily slow configuration when a faster capable worker can complete it reliably, and split broad work when that shortens the critical path without losing useful context. A lane that fails this value check should be revised, combined, split, reassigned, serialized, or omitted rather than used ceremonially.\r\n\r\n## Write-lane path-verification gate\r\n\r\nBefore launching any write-enabled subagent, the coordinator must:\r\n\r\n- resolve the current repository root and verify every assigned existing file path against that current repository;\r\n- record each assigned file using its exact canonical repository path, not shorthand, a basename alone, an inferred filename, or an unverified location;\r\n- determine whether every assigned path that does not exist is intentionally being created or remains unresolved;\r\n- label each intended new file explicitly as **intentional new-file ownership** before granting write authorization;\r\n- label each confirmed existing file explicitly as **verified existing-file ownership**;\r\n- label every unresolved or unverified path explicitly as **unresolved path â€” read-only**, and keep the affected lane read-only until verification or intentional-new-file classification is complete; and\r\n- confirm one-writer ownership and integration boundaries only after these path states are known.\r\n\r\nA directory or path pattern may define the outer ownership boundary, but it does not replace verification of each assigned existing file. Final verification\r\n\r\nBefore claiming completion:\r\n\r\n- re-read the original user request and governing sources;\r\n- map every acceptance criterion to a delivered change or verified result;\r\n- reconcile every lane output and resolve or disclose contradictions;\r\n- confirm no material agent result remains unreviewed;\r\n- inspect the complete integrated diff and working tree for accidental scope expansion;\r\n- verify shared-file ownership and handoffs are complete;\r\n- run required focused, integrated, runtime, regression, accessibility, performance, security, migration, build, or acceptance checks as applicable;\r\n- distinguish skipped, unverified, pre-existing, and failed checks;\r\n- confirm generated artifacts and unrelated work were not accidentally staged or treated as source; and\r\n- run the single coordinator-owned repository finalization gate from `AGENTS.md`.\r\n\r\nFor documentation-only work, use proportionate document validation and do not launch the application or full test suite unless a governing instruction explicitly requires it.\r\n\r\n### 24. Final report format\r\n\r\nThe coordinator reports:\r\n\r\n```text\r\nOutcome: what was completed\r\nParallel execution: lanes, modes, ownership boundaries, waves, maximum concurrency, and why the decomposition was safe/useful\r\nSubagent lifecycle: total unique workers; important results; failed, blocked, replaced, or cancelled lanes; and reconciliation/integration status\r\nParallel execution outcome for substantial tasks: effect on throughput, capacity, depth/coverage, verification, elapsed time, duplication/overhead, and improvements for the next decomposition\r\nAffected files/systems: task-authored changes, sync-owned changes, and pre-existing work classified separately\r\nValidation: commands/checks, exit status, and material evidence\r\nFailures/limitations: unresolved or skipped checks and why\r\nRemaining risks: known risks that remain within or outside scope\r\nFollow-up: only work genuinely outside the requested scope\r\nChat archive: required synchronization result\r\nDevelopment docs: required synchronization result\r\n```\r\n\r\nFor every substantial task that used subagents, include the complete final parallel-execution summary required by the communication plan: total unique subagents, maximum simultaneous workers, waves, roles and ownership boundaries, read-only and write-enabled lanes, important results from each lane, failures/blocks/replacements/cancellations, reconciliation, realized capacity/depth/coverage/verification/time benefits, avoidable duplication or overhead, and decomposition improvements. Keep the assessment concise and evidence-based. Do not claim speculative numerical percentages unless timing or work data was actually recorded.\r\n\r\nFor every substantial task, the final execution assessment must also state concisely and from observed task evidence:\r\n\r\n- whether independent work began promptly;\r\n- whether useful capacity remained unnecessarily idle;\r\n- whether critical-path work received priority;\r\n- whether completed results were reviewed and integrated promptly;\r\n- whether parallelization materially reduced elapsed time;\r\n- what avoidable waiting, duplication, or planning overhead occurred; and\r\n- how a similar future task could finish faster.\r\n\r\nDo not invent timing figures, duration estimates, or percentages that were not measured.\r\n\r\nThe report provides concise rationale, evidence, decisions, and results. It does not expose private chain-of-thought or paste raw agent logs.\r\n\r\n", "type": "input_text"}]

the same shared frontend source wherever technically possible.\\r\\n\\r\\nPlatform differences must be implemented through adapters and capability detection.\\r\\n\\r\\n## 3.2 No desktop rewrite\\r\\n\\r\\nDo not copy the website into a second independent desktop codebase.\\r\\n\\r\\nThe desktop application must package or render the same frontend application using the existing framework and shared packages.\\r\\n\\r\\n## 3.3 No model-specific coupling\\r\\n\\r\\nStory blocks and core waypoint records must not contain fields tied directly to a particular model such as LightGlue, DINOv2, COLMAP, ONNX, or a specific future vision library.\\r\\n\\r\\nModel-specific data will belong inside versioned build artifacts and runtime packages in later phases.\\r\\n\\r\\n## 3.4 Published versions are immutable\\r\\n\\r\\nA published Vision Waypoint version must never be modified in place.\\r\\n\\r\\nEditing a published waypoint creates a new draft version.\\r\\n\\r\\nStories must reference a specific immutable waypoint version.\\r\\n\\r\\n## 3.5 Mocks only at authorized external boundaries\\r\\n\\r\\nB-1 is allowed to mock:\\r\\n\\r\\n* native capture;\\r\\n* frame acquisition;\\r\\n* real visual verification;\\r\\n* real vision build jobs.\\r\\n\\r\\nB-1 must not mock:\\r\\n\\r\\n* database persistence;\\r\\n* waypoint lifecycle;\\r\\n* version creation;\\r\\n* story binding;\\r\\n* event delivery;\\r\\n* platform adapter invocation;\\r\\n* verification-attempt storage;\\r\\n* idempotency;\\r\\n* UI state;\\r\\n* feature flags;\\r\\n* capability detection;\\r\\n* protocol validation.\\r\\n\\r\\nThe mock verifier must be deterministic and clearly identified as a development implementation.\\r\\n\\r\\nDo not use random confidence scores.\\r\\n\\r\\n## 3.6 Preserve the existing experience\\r\\n\\r\\nDo not redesign or replace the existing Tall Tale interface, Player page, Captain page, Studio page, animations, story presentation, authentication, or library behavior unless a change is necessary for B-1 integration.\\r\\n\\r\\nAny required UI adjustment must visually match the existing design system.\\r\\n\\r\\n## 3.7 No prohibited game integration\\r\\n\\r\\nDo not implement:\\r\\n\\r\\n* game-process injection;\\r\\n* game-memory reading;\\r\\n* input automation;\\r\\n* game-file modification;\\r\\n* in-game overlays;\\r\\n* real game-window capture.\\r\\n\\r\\nThese belong outside B-1 or are permanently prohibited.\\r\\n\\r\\n---\\r\\n\\r\\n# 4. Mandatory Initial Repository Audit\\r\\n\\r\\nBefore implementation, inspect the repository and document:\\r\\n\\r\\n* frontend framework and version;\\r\\n* backend framework and version;\\r\\n* package manager;\\r\\n* workspace or monorepo tooling;\\r\\n* database and migration system;\\r\\n* authentication architecture;\\r\\n* Story/Tall Tale data model;\\r\\n* current Player, Captain, and Studio route structure;\\r\\n* story progression system;\\r\\n* event system;\\r\\n* existing block editor;\\r\\n* current testing frameworks;\\r\\n* current build and deployment workflows;\\r\\n* existing PWA support;\\r\\n* existing desktop or native code;\\r\\n* current API schema validation;\\r\\n* versioning conventions;\\r\\n* locations of project documentation;\\r\\n* canonical development branch and repository root;\\r\\n* uncommitted changes that must not be overwritten.\\r\\n\\r\\nCreate an implementation audit document, for example:\\r\\n\\r\\n```text\\r\\nDevelopment_Docs/\\r\\n  AR/\\r\\n    Phase_B1/\\r\\n      B1_Repository_Audit.md\\r\\n```\\r\\n\\r\\nThe audit must explain how the implementation will fit the existing system.\\r\\n\\r\\nDo not restructure the entire repository merely to match an example folder layout. Preserve existing conventions when they are sound.\\r\\n\\r\\n---\\r\\n\\r\\n# 5. Architecture Decision Records\\r\\n\\r\\nCreate ADRs for all material architecture decisions made during B-1.\\r\\n\\r\\nAt minimum, create or update ADRs covering:\\r\\n\\r\\n1. shared web and desktop application architecture;\\r\\n2. desktop framework selection;\\r\\n3. platform-adapter pattern;\\r\\n4. Vision Waypoint versioning and immutability;\\r\\n5. protocol serialization and schema validation;\\r\\n6. PWA caching boundaries;\\r\\n7. mock-verification architecture;\\r\\n8. feature-flag system;\\r\\n9. event idempotency strategy;\\r\\n10. database entity design.\\r\\n\\r\\nRecommended ADR location:\\r\\n\\r\\n```text\\r\\nDevelopment_Docs/\\r\\n  AR/\\r\\n    ADRs/\\r\\n```\\r\\n\\r\\nUse the projectâ€™s existing ADR format when one exists.\\r\\n\\r\\nEach ADR must contain:\\r\\n\\r\\n* status;\\r\\n* context;\\r\\n* decision;\\r\\n* alternatives considered;\\r\\n* consequences;\\r\\n* migration implications;\\r\\n* security implications;\\r\\n* compatibility implications.\\r\\n\\r\\n---\\r\\n\\r\\n# 6. Target Shared Architecture\\r\\n\\r\\nAdapt the existing repository toward this logical structure without forcing unnecessary renaming:\\r\\n\\r\\n```text\\r\\napps/\\r\\n  web/\\r\\n  desktop/\\r\\n  server/\\r\\n  vision-worker/             # may remain scaffolded in B-1\\r\\n\\r\\npackages/\\r\\n  ui/\\r\\n  design-system/\\r\\n  story-engine/\\r\\n  vision-waypoint-domain/\\r\\n  vision-protocol/\\r\\n  platform-adapters/\\r\\n  schemas/\\r\\n  testing-fixtures/\\r\\n\\r\\nDevelopment_Docs/\\r\\n  AR/\\r\\n    Governing_Specification/\\r\\n    Phase_B_Roadmap/\\r\\n    Phase_B1/\\r\\n    ADRs/\\r\\n```\\r\\n\\r\\nExisting code should be moved only when doing so clearly improves sharing and can be completed safely.\\r\\n\\r\\nA partial structural migration is acceptable when:\\r\\n\\r\\n* the final logical boundaries are established;\\r\\n* imports use shared packages or modules;\\r\\n* no duplicate implementations are introduced;\\r\\n* the remaining migration work is documented.\\r\\n\\r\\n---\\r\\n\\r\\n# 7. Work Package B1.1: Shared Domain Model\\r\\n\\r\\nImplement a real, persistent Vision Waypoint domain model.\\r\\n\\r\\nUse the existing database and migration framework.\\r\\n\\r\\n## 7.1 VisionWaypoint\\r\\n\\r\\nRepresents the stable identity across versions.\\r\\n\\r\\nRequired logical fields:\\r\\n\\r\\n```text\\r\\nid\\r\\nownerId\\r\\nname\\r\\ndescription\\r\\ntype\\r\\nlocationTags\\r\\nsharingScope\\r\\narchivedAt\\r\\ncreatedAt\\r\\nupdatedAt\\r\\n```\\r\\n\\r\\nSupported initial types:\\r\\n\\r\\n```text\\r\\nAREA_ARRIVAL\\r\\nEXACT_LANDMARK\\r\\nVIEWPOINT\\r\\nOBJECT_INSPECTION\\r\\nITEM_PICKUP\\r\\nSEQUENCE\\r\\nADVANCED\\r\\n```\\r\\n\\r\\nSupported sharing scopes:\\r\\n\\r\\n```text\\r\\nPRIVATE\\r\\nCREW\\r\\nTALL_TALE\\r\\nCOMMUNITY\\r\\nOFFICIAL\\r\\n```\\r\\n\\r\\nCommunity and Official publication do not need to be enabled yet, but the domain values must be supportable without schema redesign.\\r\\n\\r\\n## 7.2 VisionWaypointVersion\\r\\n\\r\\nRepresents a draft or immutable published version.\\r\\n\\r\\nRequired logical fields:\\r\\n\\r\\n```text\\r\\nid\\r\\nwaypointId\\r\\nversionNumber\\r\\nparentVersionId\\r\\nlifecycleStatus\\r\\nverificationProfile\\r\\npackageSchemaVersion\\r\\ndraftConfiguration\\r\\npackageArtifactReference\\r\\ncompatibilityMetadata\\r\\ncertificationReference\\r\\ncreatedBy\\r\\npublishedBy\\r\\ncreatedAt\\r\\nupdatedAt\\r\\npublishedAt\\r\\ndeprecatedAt\\r\\n```\\r\\n\\r\\nVerification profiles:\\r\\n\\r\\n```text\\r\\nBALANCED\\r\\nSTRICT\\r\\nSTORY_CRITICAL\\r\\nCUSTOM\\r\\n```\\r\\n\\r\\nLifecycle states must include:\\r\\n\\r\\n```text\\r\\nDRAFT\\r\\nCOLLECTING_REFERENCE_DATA\\r\\nREADY_TO_BUILD\\r\\nBUILDING\\r\\nNEEDS_ADDITIONAL_DATA\\r\\nBUILD_FAILED\\r\\nREADY_FOR_TESTING\\r\\nCALIBRATION_FAILED\\r\\nSHADOW_READY\\r\\nCAPTAIN_CONFIRMED\\r\\nAUTOMATIC\\r\\nUNSAFE\\r\\nDEPRECATED\\r\\nINCOMPATIBLE\\r\\n```\\r\\n\\r\\nB-1 does not need to use every state operationally, but the lifecycle must be modeled explicitly.\\r\\n\\r\\n## 7.3 VisionWaypointDraftConfiguration\\r\\n\\r\\nThe draft configuration must be schema-versioned.\\r\\n\\r\\nInclude logical support for:\\r\\n\\r\\n```text\\r\\nwaypoint type\\r\\nverification profile\\r\\nscan interaction settings\\r\\ncreator guidance preferences\\r\\nCaptain fallback policy\\r\\naccepted pose configuration placeholder\\r\\nstable region placeholder\\r\\nhard-negative requirement placeholder\\r\\nstory-purpose metadata\\r\\nbuild preference\\r\\n```\\r\\n\\r\\nDo not embed model-specific fields.\\r\\n\\r\\n## 7.4 VisionWaypointPublication\\r\\n\\r\\nRepresents publication metadata and immutable package identity.\\r\\n\\r\\nRequired logical fields:\\r\\n\\r\\n```text\\r\\nid\\r\\nwaypointVersionId\\r\\npackageHash\\r\\npackageSchemaVersion\\r\\npublishedAt\\r\\npublishedBy\\r\\ncompatibilityRange\\r\\nstatus\\r\\n```\\r\\n\\r\\nB-1 may use a mock package hash and development package artifact, but publication rules must be real.\\r\\n\\r\\n## 7.5 StoryWaypointBinding\\r\\n\\r\\nConnects a story block to one immutable waypoint version.\\r\\n\\r\\nRequired logical fields:\\r\\n\\r\\n```text\\r\\nid\\r\\nstoryId\\r\\nstageId or blockId\\r\\nwaypointId\\r\\nwaypointVersionId\\r\\nruntimeMode\\r\\nscanInteraction\\r\\nsuccessEvent\\r\\nretryMessageConfiguration\\r\\nfailureMessageConfiguration\\r\\nCaptainFallbackPolicy\\r\\nofflineBehavior\\r\\ncreatedAt\\r\\nupdatedAt\\r\\n```\\r\\n\\r\\nRuntime modes:\\r\\n\\r\\n```text\\r\\nDEVELOPMENT_MOCK\\r\\nSHADOW\\r\\nCAPTAIN_CONFIRMED\\r\\nAUTOMATIC\\r\\n```\\r\\n\\r\\nB-1 only permits `DEVELOPMENT_MOCK`.\\r\\n\\r\\n## 7.6 VerificationAttempt\\r\\n\\r\\nPersist mock and future runtime attempts.\\r\\n\\r\\nRequired logical fields:\\r\\n\\r\\n```text\\r\\nid\\r\\nstoryId\\r\\nstageId\\r\\nplayerId\\r\\nwaypointId\\r\\nwaypointVersionId\\r\\nattemptState\\r\\nresult\\r\\nguidanceCode\\r\\nevidenceDigest\\r\\nplatform\\r\\nadapterType\\r\\neventDeliveryStatus\\r\\nCaptainAction\\r\\ncreatedAt\\r\\nstartedAt\\r\\ncompletedAt\\r\\nclosedAt\\r\\n```\\r\\n\\r\\nAttempt results:\\r\\n\\r\\n```text\\r\\nVERIFIED\\r\\nINSUFFICIENT_VISUAL_EVIDENCE\\r\\nNOT_AT_TARGET\\r\\nAMBIGUOUS\\r\\nSYSTEM_ERROR\\r\\nCANCELLED\\r\\n```\\r\\n\\r\\nB-1 mock scenarios must support every result.\\r\\n\\r\\n## 7.7 CompanionDevice and PairingSession\\r\\n\\r\\nCreate the initial domain representation needed for future browser-to-Companion pairing.\\r\\n\\r\\nCompanionDevice logical fields:\\r\\n\\r\\n```text\\r\\nid\\r\\nownerId\\r\\ndisplayName\\r\\ninstanceId\\r\\nprotocolVersion\\r\\ncapabilities\\r\\nlastSeenAt\\r\\nrevokedAt\\r\\ncreatedAt\\r\\n```\\r\\n\\r\\nPairingSession logical fields:\\r\\n\\r\\n```text\\r\\nid\\r\\nownerId\\r\\ncompanionDeviceId\\r\\npairingCodeHash\\r\\nsessionSecretHash\\r\\nallowedOrigin\\r\\nexpiresAt\\r\\npairedAt\\r\\nrevokedAt\\r\\ncreatedAt\\r\\n```\\r\\n\\r\\nB-1 does not need to expose a real localhost service, but the contract and persistence model must be ready.\\r\\n\\r\\n## 7.8 Migration quality\\r\\n\\r\\nDatabase migrations must:\\r\\n\\r\\n* be reversible where the existing migration system supports reversal;\\r\\n* preserve all current project data;\\r\\n* include indexes for common queries;\\r\\n* include foreign keys and uniqueness constraints;\\r\\n* prevent multiple conflicting published version numbers;\\r\\n* prevent story bindings from referencing nonexistent versions;\\r\\n* avoid storing derived status redundantly when it can become contradictory;\\r\\n* include seed or fixture data for B-1 testing.\\r\\n\\r\\nCreate migration tests where the current project supports them.\\r\\n\\r\\n---\\r\\n\\r\\n# 8. Work Package B1.2: Versioning and Lifecycle Services\\r\\n\\r\\nImplement application services that enforce lifecycle rules.\\r\\n\\r\\nRequired operations:\\r\\n\\r\\n```text\\r\\ncreateWaypoint\\r\\nupdateWaypointMetadata\\r\\narchiveWaypoint\\r\\ncreateDraftVersion\\r\\nupdateDraftConfiguration\\r\\npublishDraftVersion\\r\\ndeprecatePublishedVersion\\r\\ngetLatestDraft\\r\\ngetPublishedVersions\\r\\ngetWaypointUsage\\r\\nbindWaypointVersionToStory\\r\\nreplaceStoryWaypointBinding\\r\\n```\\r\\n\\r\\nMandatory rules:\\r\\n\\r\\n* only draft versions may be edited;\\r\\n* publishing seals the version;\\r\\n* publication must create or preserve a package hash;\\r\\n* published versions are immutable;\\r\\n* creating a new draft from a published version copies allowed configuration and records `parentVersionId`;\\r\\n* deprecating a version does not delete it;\\r\\n* stories retain access to pinned deprecated versions unless explicitly migrated;\\r\\n* replacing a binding is explicit and audited;\\r\\n* archive operations cannot destroy historical bindings.\\r\\n\\r\\nAdd domain-level tests for all rules.\\r\\n\\r\\n---\\r\\n\\r\\n# 9. Work Package B1.3: Vision Protocol Package\\r\\n\\r\\nCreate a versioned shared protocol package used by:\\r\\n\\r\\n* web application;\\r\\n* desktop application;\\r\\n* mock verifier;\\r\\n* future Companion;\\r\\n* future vision worker;\\r\\n* server APIs.\\r\\n\\r\\nUse the projectâ€™s existing validation technology when suitable, such as JSON Schema, Zod, Pydantic, TypeBox, generated OpenAPI schemas, or an equivalent.\\r\\n\\r\\nDo not define important messages only as informal TypeScript interfaces without runtime validation.\\r\\n\\r\\n## 9.1 Common envelope\\r\\n\\r\\nEvery protocol message must contain:\\r\\n\\r\\n```json\\r\\n{\\r\\n  \\\"protocolVersion\\\": \\\"1.0\\\",\\r\\n  \\\"messageType\\\": \\\"string\\\",\\r\\n  \\\"messageId\\\": \\\"unique-id\\\",\\r\\n  \\\"requestId\\\": \\\"optional-related-request-id\\\",\\r\\n  \\\"sessionId\\\": \\\"session-id\\\",\\r\\n  \\\"timestamp\\\": \\\"ISO-8601 timestamp\\\",\\r\\n  \\\"sender\\\": {\\r\\n    \\\"type\\\": \\\"web|desktop|companion|vision-worker|server\\\",\\r\\n    \\\"instanceId\\\": \\\"instance-id\\\"\\r\\n  },\\r\\n  \\\"payload\\\": {}\\r\\n}\\r\\n```\\r\\n\\r\\n## 9.2 Required message families\\r\\n\\r\\nDefine and validate schemas for:\\r\\n\\r\\n```text\\r\\ncompanion.hello\\r\\ncompanion.capabilities\\r\\ncompanion.pair.request\\r\\ncompanion.pair.approved\\r\\ncompanion.pair.rejected\\r\\ncompanion.status\\r\\n\\r\\ncapture.target.select.request\\r\\ncapture.target.selected\\r\\ncapture.target.unavailable\\r\\n\\r\\ncapture.creator.start\\r\\ncapture.creator.progress\\r\\ncapture.creator.complete\\r\\ncapture.creator.cancel\\r\\ncapture.creator.failed\\r\\n\\r\\nruntime.scan.start\\r\\nruntime.scan.progress\\r\\nruntime.scan.cancel\\r\\nruntime.scan.result\\r\\nruntime.scan.failed\\r\\n\\r\\nbuild.request\\r\\nbuild.progress\\r\\nbuild.complete\\r\\nbuild.failed\\r\\n\\r\\nvision.pause\\r\\nvision.resume\\r\\n\\r\\ndiagnostic.bundle.request\\r\\ndiagnostic.bundle.available\\r\\n```\\r\\n\\r\\nB-1 only needs to execute mock runtime-scan messages, but all core families should have initial schemas.\\r\\n\\r\\n## 9.3 Capability schema\\r\\n\\r\\nSupport capability reporting for:\\r\\n\\r\\n```text\\r\\nnativeCapture\\r\\nglobalHotkeys\\r\\nlocalInference\\r\\ncloudBuild\\r\\nofflinePackages\\r\\nsystemTray\\r\\ndiagnosticRetention\\r\\nhardwareProviders\\r\\nsupportedProtocolVersions\\r\\nsupportedPackageSchemaVersions\\r\\n```\\r\\n\\r\\n## 9.4 Error codes\\r\\n\\r\\nDefine governed error codes rather than returning arbitrary strings.\\r\\n\\r\\nAt minimum:\\r\\n\\r\\n```text\\r\\nCOMPANION_UNAVAILABLE\\r\\nPAIRING_REQUIRED\\r\\nPAIRING_EXPIRED\\r\\nORIGIN_NOT_ALLOWED\\r\\nCAPTURE_PERMISSION_DENIED\\r\\nCAPTURE_TARGET_UNAVAILABLE\\r\\nPACKAGE_MISSING\\r\\nPACKAGE_INCOMPATIBLE\\r\\nMODEL_UNAVAILABLE\\r\\nHARDWARE_UNSUPPORTED\\r\\nATTEMPT_STALE\\r\\nSTORY_STAGE_CHANGED\\r\\nVALIDATION_FAILED\\r\\nMOCK_SCENARIO_NOT_FOUND\\r\\nINTERNAL_ERROR\\r\\n```\\r\\n\\r\\n## 9.5 Contract tests\\r\\n\\r\\nAdd tests that:\\r\\n\\r\\n* validate every example message;\\r\\n* reject invalid protocol versions;\\r\\n* reject missing required envelope fields;\\r\\n* reject unknown enum values where strictness is required;\\r\\n* verify serialization/deserialization in both web and server runtimes;\\r\\n* verify desktop compatibility;\\r\\n* protect against accidental schema drift.\\r\\n\\r\\n---\\r\\n\\r\\n# 10. Prohibited Shortcuts\\r\\n\\r\\nDo not:\\r\\n\\r\\n* hard-code the userâ€™s machine paths;\\r\\n* hard-code one Sea of Thieves window handle;\\r\\n* select a window silently;\\r\\n* capture the full display by default;\\r\\n* save player scans because disk storage is easier;\\r\\n* send raw full-resolution frames through JSON;\\r\\n* send frames to the production server;\\r\\n* claim blur analysis is location verification;\\r\\n* return `VERIFIED`;\\r\\n* build B-4 models prematurely;\\r\\n* place capture logic directly in React components;\\r\\n* duplicate capture code between web and desktop;\\r\\n* create a generic unauthenticated localhost server;\\r\\n* use wildcard CORS;\\r\\n* log pairing tokens;\\r\\n* expose arbitrary file operations;\\r\\n* create an in-game overlay;\\r\\n* read game memory;\\r\\n* automate game input;\\r\\n* use capture failure as a story rejection;\\r\\n* skip testing because the preview looked correct;\\r\\n* close the phase with a mock capture source;\\r\\n* mutate Phase B-1 architecture without an ADR;\\r\\n* turn implementation tasks into additional top-level phases.\\r\\n\\r\\n---\\r\\n\\r\\n# 40. Quality Standard\\r\\n\\r\\nThe final result should feel like a trustworthy product capability rather than a developer experiment.\\r\\n\\r\\nA successful Phase B-2 means:\\r\\n\\r\\n* capture begins verification exists.\\r\\n\\r\\nImplement the complete phase, run the full test program, perform the required demonstrations, update the documentation, and provide the Phase B-2 completion report.\\r\\n\\r\\nDo not stop after scaffolding.\\r\\n\\r\\nDo not leave critical operations as TODOs.\\r\\n\\r\\nDo not replace required behavior with decorative UI.\\r\\n\\r\\nPhase B-2 is complete Patch\";\nCodex_Chats/chats/019f737e-a458-7c10-afec-b6a7b51c8881--implement-phase-b-1-foundation.md:8251:[{\"text\": \"Script completed\\nWall time 0.3 seconds\\nOutput:\\n\", \"type\": \"input_text\"}, {\"text\": \"Exit code: 0\\nWall time: 0.2 seconds\\nOutput:\\n# ADR 0011: Electron window capture and one Companion coordinator\\r\\n\\r\\nStatus: accepted for Phase B-2\\r\\n\\r\\n## Context\\r\\n\\r\\nB-1 selected Electron because the shared application requires a dynamic Next.js/Prisma server and the host had no Rust toolchain. B-2 requires real user-selected Windows application-window capture for both the integrated desktop and a paired browser without duplicating capture code or moving native logic into React.\\r\\n\\r\\nElectron exposes Windows application windows through main-process `desktopCapturer` sources and captures an approved source through Chromium media APIs. A source ID contains the HWND on Windows. This is a supported, read-only individual-window capture path and does not modify the source application.\\r\\n\\r\\n## Decision\\r\\n\\r\\nCreate one `CompanionCoordinator` and one `CaptureCore` in the Electron main process. A dedicated hidden, sandboxed capture worker owns the media stream and MediaRecorder. It receives only a selected `window:*` source ID. It sends downscaled binary frame buffers and bounded recording chunks to the coordinator.\\r\\n\\r\\nDesktop IPC and browser WebSocket adapters call the same coordinator commands. Target enumeration and selection occur in the main process and return sanitized candidate metadata plus small thumbnails only after an explicit user action. The app never selects a likely Sea of Thieves source silently and never offers full-display capture by default.\\r\\n\\r\\nThe capability report names the API `ELECTRON_DESKTOP_CAPTURER`. It does not assert that a particular internal Chromium capture backend is active.\\r\\n\\r\\n## Alternatives considered\\r\\n\\r\\n- Tauri/Rust Windows Graphics Capture: rejected because Rust is absent and B-1 already chose Electron for the same shared application.\\r\\n- A new C# Windows service: rejected because no .NET SDK is installed and it would add a second build, update, and signing boundary.\\r\\n- Capture in the shared React component: rejected because it would mix UI, platform, lifecycle, privacy, and resource ownership.\\r\\n- Separate desktop and browser capture implementations: prohibited because behavior and security would drift.\\r\\n- Full-display capture fallback: rejected because it expands privacy scope beyond the selected game window.\\r\\n\\r\\n## Consequences\\r\\n\\r\\nCapture has one lifecycle, quality pipeline, ring buffer, storage policy, error catalog, and test harness. Electron remains the local Companion process. A hidden renderer/GPU process can fail without corrupting Studio persistence; the coordinator detects loss, clears transient frames, and requires a safe restart.\\r\\n\\r\\n## Security implications\\r\\n\\r\\nThe worker is sandboxed, has no Node integration, and accepts commands only from the coordinator. UI renderers cannot send worker events. Source IDs are validated as Windows window IDs and checked against the current enumerated candidate set. No arbitrary media, filesystem, process, or display command is exposed.\\r\\n\\r\\n## Compatibility implications\\r\\n\\r\\nThe architecture is Windows-only for B-2. Future capture backends may implement the same `CaptureWorker` and `TargetProvider` interfaces without changing shared UI or protocol contracts.\\r\\n# ADR 0012: Challenge-authenticated loopback Companion pairing\\r\\n\\r\\nStatus: accepted for Phase B-2\\r\\n\\r\\n## Context\\r\\n\\r\\nBrowser/PWA surfaces need the same local capture core as the desktop application. A generic localhost API would let unrelated websites probe or operate capture. Browsers cannot add an Authorization header during the WebSocket upgrade, and putting a bearer token in the URL would leak it into logs and diagnostics.\\r\\n\\r\\n## Decision\\r\\n\\r\\nBind an HTTP/WebSocket service only to `127.0.0.1`. Accept only exact configured origins. Pairing is an explicit two-surface ceremony:\\r\\n\\r\\n1. an allowed browser origin creates a short-lived pending request;\\r\\n2. the desktop Companion displays the origin and a random code;\\r\\n3. the user enters that code in the browser;\\r\\n4. the Companion returns a session ID and secret once;\\r\\n5. the WebSocket sends a fresh challenge;\\r\\n6. the browser proves possession with HMAC-SHA-256 over the challenge, session, origin, and protocol;\\r\\n7. every command then uses a unique request ID and strictly increasing sequence.\\r\\n\\r\\nPersist only hashes, expiration, approved origin, device identity, and revocation state. Keep the raw secret in browser session memory only. Reject used challenges, duplicate request IDs, non-increasing sequences, stale sessions, incompatible protocols, oversized messages, disallowed origins, and rate-limit violations.\\r\\n\\r\\nDesktop integration bypasses browser pairing but still uses the same protocol schema and coordinator allowlist through private IPC.\\r\\n\\r\\n## Alternatives considered\\r\\n\\r\\n- Wildcard CORS or unauthenticated localhost: prohibited.\\r\\n- Bearer token in WebSocket URL: rejected because URLs are routinely logged.\\r\\n- Long-lived pairing code: rejected because it is replayable and brute-forceable.\\r\\n- Automatic origin approval: rejected because capture must not begin without visible user awareness.\\r\\n- Remote/LAN binding: outside B-2 and requires a separate threat model.\\r\\n\\r\\n## Consequences\\r\\n\\r\\nPairing can expire and be revoked without restarting the Companion. A captured authentication proof cannot be replayed on a new connection because the challenge changes. A stolen raw session secret remains a credential, so it is short-lived, origin-bound, never logged, and not persisted in plaintext.\\r\\n\\r\\n## Security implications\\r\\n\\r\\nThe browser protocol exposes typed capture operations, managed artifact preview/delete, status, privacy, and diagnostics only. It exposes no arbitrary file path, command execution, shell, full-resolution frame stream, or unrestricted preview endpoint.\\r\\n\\r\\n## Compatibility implications\\r\\n\\r\\nCapture protocol 2.0 is negotiated explicitly. B-1 protocol 1.0 remains intact for its deterministic development verifier and is not silently upgraded.\\r\\n# ADR 0013: Scoped Windows hotkey and selected-window health monitor\\r\\n\\r\\nStatus: accepted for Phase B-2\\r\\n\\r\\n## Context\\r\\n\\r\\nElectron's `globalShortcut` reports activation and registration conflict but does not expose key release. B-2 requires press-and-hold initiation, release-to-finalize, repeat suppression, conflict reporting, and selected-window minimize/close/resize health. The Windows capture source ID includes the HWND, but Electron does not expose `IsIconic` or the target client rectangle.\\r\\n\\r\\nThe audited host has PowerShell 5.1 and .NET Framework compilation support but no Rust, C++, or .NET SDK.\\r\\n\\r\\n## Decision\\r\\n\\r\\nShip a fixed PowerShell sidecar that compiles one source-controlled C# Win32 interop surface in memory with `Add-Type`. It uses:\\r\\n\\r\\n- `RegisterHotKey` with `MOD_NOREPEAT` to detect conflicts;\\r\\n- `GetAsyncKeyState` to poll only the configured trigger key and required modifiers for down/up state;\\r\\n- `IsWindow`, `IsIconic`, and `GetClientRect` for the selected HWND;\\r\\n- a message loop and bounded health heartbeat;\\r\\n- newline-delimited, fixed-shape JSON over standard output.\\r\\n\\r\\nThe Electron coordinator launches it hidden with a fixed script path and validated numeric arguments. There is no generic script, command, or process-launch API. The monitor emits no typed text, scan code, full window title, or unrelated key event.\\r\\n\\r\\nElectron's own `globalShortcut` registration remains the first conflict check where practical. The UI also provides a local mouse/keyboard hold button and toggle accessibility mode, so native monitoring can be disabled.\\r\\n\\r\\n## Alternatives considered\\r\\n\\r\\n- Electron `globalShortcut` only: rejected because release cannot end the scan.\\r\\n- Polling all keyboard state from JavaScript: rejected because Electron exposes no safe global key-state API. The fixed monitor polls only the chosen preset.\\r\\n- Native npm keyboard-hook dependency: rejected because it adds ABI-specific binaries and rebuild/signing risk to Electron 41.\\r\\n- Input injection or game binding: prohibited.\\r\\n- Logging the full keyboard stream: prohibited and unnecessary.\\r\\n\\r\\n## Consequences\\r\\n\\r\\nThe monitor is Windows-only and may be blocked by local application-control policy. Such a block is a truthful `HOTKEY_UNAVAILABLE` state; it does not disable the in-application control. The process is terminated on hotkey disable, Companion shutdown, or app exit. A maximum scan duration and coordinator cleanup cover lost release events.\\r\\n\\r\\n## Security implications\\r\\n\\r\\nThe monitor has no administrator requirement, does not attach to the game, does not inject a DLL, does not synthesize input, and does not consume the keystroke. Only an allowlisted preset's modifier/key combination is accepted by the coordinator.\\r\\n\\r\\n## Compatibility implications\\r\\n\\r\\nFuture signed native helpers may replace the script behind the same `HotkeyService` and `TargetHealthProvider` interfaces. Public distribution still requires signing and reputation testing in Phase B-6.\\r\\n\", \"type\": \"input_text\"}]\nrg: Codex_Chats/chats/019f737e-a458-7c10-afec-b6a7-3f24780cb2d6--build-player-companion-shell.md: The system cannot find the file specified. Phase Mission\r\n\r\nImplement the complete **Native Companion and Capture Runtime** required for future Vision Waypoint authoring and player verification.\r\n\r\nAt the end of Phase B-2:\r\n\r\n* the Windows desktop application can select and capture the Sea of Thieves window;\r\n* the browser version can securely pair with the local Companion;\r\n* both browser and desktop surfaces can invoke the same shared capture operations;\r\n* creator recordings can be captured and persisted as structured recording sessions;\r\n* player hold-to-scan attempts can capture a short multi-frame scan;\r\n* runtime scan frames remain transient by default;\r\n* frame quality and scan health are analyzed without performing location recognition;\r\n* capture state, progress, errors, and evidence metadata travel through versioned contracts;\r\n* the system responds correctly to resizing, minimizing, closing, changing displays, and capture interruption;\r\n* users always know when capture is active;\r\n* unauthorized browser origins cannot access the Companion;\r\n* no game process injection, memory reading, input automation, or in-game overlay exists;\r\n* a complete mock verification request can travel from the Player interface to the Companion and back without pretending that real visual verification has occurred.\r\n\r\nThe system must be stable enough that Phase B-3 can use it for waypoint-authoring recordings and Phase B-4 can consume its scan-evidence bundles.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 3. B‐2: Native Companion and Capture Runtime 8.1 Phase mission Build the native, privacy-conscious bridge that can observe the explicitly selected Sea of Thieves window, gather creator recordings, perform player hold-to-scan capture, and communicate with the website or desktop shell through authenti- cated local contracts. This phase produces trustworthy visual evidence but does not decide whether the scene is correct. At completion, both the browser/PW A and Windows desktop application will be able to initiate a real capture session, receive frame-quality and scan metadata, and safely stop or recover from capture interruptions. 8.2 Why capture is a separate phase The capture layer is a security, privacy, reliability, and performance subsystem in its own right. Mixing it immediately with machine-learning decisions makes it difficult to distinguish: • bad frames from bad models; • a frozen capture source from a negative visual result; • a browser pairing failure from an inference failure; • insufficient scene motion from an incorrect location; • native-driver instability from story-engine behavior. B-2 SHALL make capture observable and testable before B-4 is allowed to judge it. 8.3 In scope • native Windows Companion service; • desktop integration and browser pairing; • user-selected game-window capture; • creator recording sessions; • player hold-to-scan sessions; • configurable hotkey; • transient ring buffer; • frame normalization; • capture-quality analysis; • recording-session metadata; • privacy controls and indicators; • capability discovery; • hardware and performance diagnostics; • secure localhost protocol; 22\r\nPDFPAGE 48 VISION WAYPOINT PHASE B IMPLEMENTATION ROADMAP v1.0 8.21 B‐2 required demonstration The demonstration SHALL show: 1. Studio records and previews a creator target recording; 5. Player initiates a five-second hold-to-scan; 6. the UI receives live scan progress; 7. the Companion returns a structured quality summary and selected-frame metadata; 8. no Player frames remain on disk after completion; 9. resizing or temporarily losing the window produces safe recovery behavior; 10. the same scan can be initiated in desktop-integrated mode; 11. a mock verification result continues through the B-1 story path. 8.22 B‐2 exit gate Phase B‐2 Exit Gate Phase B-2 is complete when capture, recording, scan initiation, frame lifecycle, pairing, privacy, quality measurement, failure recovery, and adapter integration are real and tested. The result may still use a mock location decision, but it must be based on a genuine structured scan produced by the selected game window. 8.22.1 Mandatory acceptance checklist □ Sea of Thieves window can be explicitly selected. □ Creator recordings are categorized and persisted safely. □ Player scans use a bounded transient ring buffer. □ Player frames are not written to disk by default. □ Hold-to-scan progress reflects real capture state. □ Frame quality and best-frame selection are implemented. □ Browser pairing is authenticated, origin-restricted, expiring, and revocable. □ Desktop mode uses the same capability contract. □ Capture stops cleanly on logout, close, source loss, and revocation. □ Resolution changes and source failure produce clear states. □ Diagnostic metadata is useful without exposing fram\r\n", "type": "input_text"}]
