stop capture and clear the transient buffer;\r\n• is replaced by a new process/window - require confirmation or an approved safe reconnection rule;\r\n• enters a capture-incompatible fullscreen mode - The duration remains\r\nwaypoint-configurable within governed limits.\r\nHotkey down\r\n-> initialize scan session\r\n-> begin buffering and progress events\r\n-> capture at configured rate\r\n-> monitor quality and motion\r\nHotkey release or maximum duration\r\n-> finalize capture\r\n-> select best frames\r\n-> clear unnecessary frames\r\n-> emit scan evidence metadata\r\n8.8.2 Required scan behavior\r\n• very short accidental presses are canceled without error;\r\n• the scan may finish automatically at the maximum duration;\r\n• the UI displays real capture state, not a fake timer;\r\n• the user can cancel;\r\n• repeated scans obey a small configurable cooldown to prevent accidental spam;\r\n• only one scan may own the selected capture source at a time;\r\n• creator recording and player scan conflicts are handled explicitly;\r\n• loss of the game window cancels the scan safely;\r\n• the scan includes enough frame timing to support future sequence analysis.\r\n8.9 B‐2 work hotkey state must be visible and disableable;\r\n25\r\n\r\n--- PDF PAGE 43 ---\r\nVISION WAYPOINT PHASE B IMPLEMENTATION ROADMAP v1.0\r\n• accessibility options should support toggle-to-scan as an alternative to hold where appropriate, while preserving ex-\r\nplicit user initiation.\r\n8.10 B‐2 work package 6: Ring buffer and frame lifecycle\r\n8.10.1 Ring‐buffer intent\r\nMaintain a bounded in-memory collection sufficient for:\r\n• the active scan window;\r\n• a small pre-roll to avoid losing the first useful view;\r\n• frame-quality selection;\r\n• short recovery from capture jitter.\r\n8.10.2 Frame lifecycle rules\r\nCaptured frame\r\n-> transient memory buffer\r\n-> normalized candidate\r\n-> quality metadata\r\n-> selected evidence frame or discarded\r\n-> vision worker in later phases\r\n-> erased after result unless retention consent exists\r\nNo continuous disk recording is permitted in Player mode by default.\r\n8.10.3 Resource limits\r\nThe Companion MUST enforce:\r\n• maximum frame count;\r\n• maximum memory budget;\r\n• maximum scan duration;\r\n• downscaled analysis resolution;\r\n• backpressure if processing falls behind;\r\n• frame-dropping strategy that preserves temporal distribution rather than only the newest frames.\r\n8.11 B‐2 work package 7: Frame normalization\r\nThe capture layer SHOULD produce normalized evidence with metadata, not silently destructive transformations.\r\nOperations may include:\r\n• color-space conversion;\r\n• alpha removal;\r\n• resolution downscaling;\r\n• letterbox or crop metadata;\r\n• HUD-safe-region metadata;\r\n• timestamp normalization;\r\n• orientation confirmation;\r\n• duplicate hashing;\r\n• optional multiple scales for later analysis.\r\n26\r\n\r\n--- PDF PAGE 44 ---\r\nVISION WAYPOINT Capture‐quality service\r\nEach frame SHOULD receive objective measurements for:\r\n• sharpness and motion blur;\r\n• brightness and clipping;\r\n• contrast;\r\n• near-duplicate similarity;\r\n• percentage dominated by sky, water, or near-uniform regions where feasible;\r\n• obstruction or UI/menu likelihood;\r\n• estimated camera motion relative to adjacent frames;\r\n• temporal spacing;\r\n• corruption or incomplete-frame detection.\r\nThe scan summary SHOULD include:\r\n{\r\n\"capturedFrameCount\": 52,\r\n\"usableFrameCount\": 12,\r\n\"selectedFrameCount\": 9,\r\n\"averageSharpness\": 0.83,\r\n\"brightnessStatus\": \"acceptable\",\r\n\"motionStatus\": \"good_slow_scan\",\r\n\"duplicateRate\": 0.31,\r\n\"captureContinuity\": 0.97\r\n}\r\nThese values do not decide the location. They decide whether the evidence is suitable for later judgment.\r\n8.13 B‐2 work package 9: Best‐frame selection\r\nThe phase SHALL implement deterministic best-frame selection using capture quality and temporal diversity. Selected\r\nframes should:\r\n• avoid severe blur;\r\n• cover the full scan time;\r\n• include different viewpoints;\r\n• avoid near duplicates;\r\n• preserve at least several connected adjacent frames for temporal analysis;\r\n• remain within a bounded count appropriate for later inference.\r\nThe selection algorithm and its version MUST be recorded in scan metadata.\r\n8.14 B‐2 work package 10: Browser pairing and localhost security\r\n8.14.1 Pairing flow\r\n1. user launches the Companion;\r\n2. [{"text": "Script completed\nWall time 0.5 seconds\nOutput:\n", "type": "input_text"}, {"text": "Exit code: 0\nWall time: 0.4 seconds\nOutput:\n# ADR 0001: Shared web, PWA, and desktop application\n\nStatus: accepted for Phase B-1\n\n## Context\n\nPlayer, Captain, and Studio already share one Next.js App Router application, domain model, design system, API, and story engine. Phase B requires browser, PWA, and Windows delivery without divergent products.\n\n## Decision\n\nKeep the current Next.js application as the canonical product. The PWA registers against it, and the desktop shell packages and launches its production standalone output. No Player, Captain, Studio, authentication, or story implementation is copied into a second frontend.\n\n## Alternatives considered\n\n- Split the repository into several applications immediately: rejected because it would move stable code without improving the B-1 vertical slice.\n- Build a separate desktop React application: rejected because it would drift and violate the governing shared-product rule.\n\n## Consequences\n\nAll surfaces inherit the same routes and UI changes. Desktop packaging includes the application server runtime as well as frontend assets.\n\n## Migration implications\n\nShared Vision modules are added under `src/vision`; a future monorepo extraction may preserve these boundaries without changing contracts.\n\n## Security implications\n\nDesktop content remains local, while authentication, authorization, CSRF, and server validation remain unchanged.\n\n## Compatibility implications\n\nExisting browser routes and deployments continue to work. Desktop-specific behavior is available only through the adapter and allowlisted preload bridge.\n\r\n# ADR 0002: Electron desktop shell\n\nStatus: accepted for Phase B-1\n\n## Context\n\nTauri 2 is preferred when a frontend can be bundled as static assets or paired with a justified sidecar. This repository uses dynamic Next.js server components, route handlers, Prisma, database-backed sessions, and filesystem-backed assets. The audited Windows host has Node but no Rust toolchain. Tauri would still require a bundled Node server sidecar.\n\n## Decision\n\nUse Electron as a narrow Windows shell. It launches the packaged Next standalone server on loopback, renders that local application, uses one-instance locking, disables renderer Node integration, enables context isolation and sandboxing, and exposes only fixed IPC commands through a preload bridge.\n\n## Alternatives considered\n\n- Tauri 2 plus Node sidecar: rejected for B-1 because it adds Rust and Node native packaging while retaining the same server requirement.\n- Remote production URL wrapper: prohibited because it is not a local production bundle.\n- Static export: rejected because it cannot preserve the existing authenticated dynamic application.\n\n## Consequences\n\nThe artifact is larger than Tauri but uses one existing runtime family and packages the actual application. Electron-builder becomes a development dependency.\n\n## Migration implications\n\nThe `VisionPlatformAdapter` contract permits a future shell substitution. No domain or UI type depends on Electron.\n\n## Security implications\n\nNo generic shell, filesystem, process, or arbitrary IPC command is exposed. Navigation and window creation are restricted, and production loads only the owned loopback server.\n\n## Compatibility implications\n\nThe development shell uses the normal Next development URL; production uses bundled standalone output and does not require a separately installed development server.\n\r\n# ADR 0003: Vision platform adapters\n\nStatus: accepted for Phase B-1\n\n## Context\n\nThe shared UI must work in browser, PWA, and desktop environments while future native capture remains outside B-1.\n\n## Decision\n\nDefine one `VisionPlatformAdapter` contract and select `MockVisionPlatformAdapter`, `WebCompanionPlatformAdapter`, or `DesktopPlatformAdapter` through a factory. Components depend only on the contract. Desktop bridge calls and future localhost communication stay inside adapters.\n\n## Alternatives considered\n\n- Platform checks inside React components: rejected because capability behavior would scatter.\n- A single adapter with optional methods: rejected because unavailable and incompatible states would become ambiguous.\n\n## Consequences\n\nCapability reporting and error behavior are explicit and testable. B-2 can replace an adapter without redesigning UI or story logic.\n\n## Migration implications\n\nExisting helper APIs remain compatible and may later back a Companion adapter.\n\n## Security implications\n\nNative APIs are never imported by shared UI. Capability truth prevents a browser from pretending native capture exists.\n\n## Compatibility implications\n\nAll adapters consume the same versioned protocol and return the same governed results.\n\r\n# ADR 0004: Vision Waypoint version immutability\n\nStatus: accepted for Phase B-1\n\n## Context\n\nOne reusable waypoint may serve many stories. Editing a published version in place would silently change active and historical playthrough behavior.\n\n## Decision\n\nSeparate stable `VisionWaypoint` identity from numbered `VisionWaypointVersion` records. Only unpublished draft versions are editable. Publication creates a one-to-one immutable publication record, deterministic package artifact and SHA-256 hash. New work derives a draft with `parentVersionId`. Story bindings pin the exact published version.\n\n## Alternatives considered\n\n- Store the latest configuration on the stable waypoint: rejected because stories would float.\n- Copy configuration into every story only: rejected because reuse, usage lookup, and governed package identity would be lost.\n\n## Consequences\n\nEdits require explicit new drafts and story migration. Deprecated versions remain resolvable.\n\n## Migration implications\n\nThe schema is additive and does not modify existing Tall Tale publication rows.\n\n## Security implications\n\nPublication and binding require server authorization. Artifact hashes detect modified development packages.\n\n## Compatibility implications\n\nPackage schema and compatibility metadata are versioned independently of database migrations.\n\r\n# ADR 0005: Zod protocol serialization and validation\n\nStatus: accepted for Phase B-1\n\n## Context\n\nVision messages will cross web, desktop, Companion, worker, and server boundaries. TypeScript-only interfaces provide no runtime protection.\n\n## Decision\n\nUse strict Zod schemas as the canonical protocol implementation. A versioned common envelope, discriminated message types, capabilities, governed errors, package manifests, and examples are shared by all B-1 runtimes. JSON remains the wire format.\n\n## Alternatives considered\n\n- Informal interfaces: rejected because invalid runtime messages would pass unchecked.\n- A second schema technology: rejected because Zod is already a core repository dependency and route convention.\n\n## Consequences\n\nSchemas provide inferred TypeScript types and runtime parsing. Contract snapshots guard drift.\n\n## Migration implications\n\nProtocol major/minor compatibility is separate from application/database versioning.\n\n## Security implications\n\nUnknown types, versions, enum values, and unrecognized fields fail closed at boundaries.\n\n## Compatibility implications\n\nExamples are plain JSON and can be validated by future non-TypeScript implementations against generated JSON Schema/OpenAPI documentation.\n\r\n# ADR 0006: PWA cache boundaries\n\nStatus: accepted for Phase B-1\n\n## Context\n\nAn installable offline shell is required, but stale authenticated or mutable data would misrepresent story truth and leak sensitive state.\n\n## Decision\n\nUse a versioned service-worker cache with an explicit static allowlist. Cache the offline document, manifest, icons, same-origin hashed `/_next/static/*` assets, and approved public assets. Treat `/api/*`, authentication, Player/Captain/Studio data, attempts, pairing, and mutable navigation as network-only. Navigations use network-first with offline fallback.\n\n## Alternatives considered\n\n- Cache-first for all GET requests: rejected as unsafe.\n- No service worker: rejected because it cannot satisfy installability and offline-shell requirements.\n\n## Consequences\n\nThe shell can open offline while protected live content truthfully reports unavailable. Cache version and update state are exposed in diagnostics.\n\n## Migration implications\n\nLater downloaded story packages require a separate versioned cache and explicit user action.\n\n## Security implications\n\nSensitive mutable responses never enter Cache Storage. Logout does not rely on cache eviction for secrecy.\n\n## Compatibility implications\n\nUnsupported browsers continue as normal web applications without false install status.\n\r\n# ADR 0007: Deterministic mock verification\n\nStatus: accepted for Phase B-1\n\n## Context\n\nB-1 authorizes mocks only for capture and visual inference. Persistence, adapter invocation, protocol validation, lifecycle, stale checks, and event delivery must be real.\n\n## Decision\n\nImplement named deterministic scenarios with fixed result/guidance mappings and a stable SHA-256 evidence digest. The adapter sends real protocol envelopes, the server persists attempts/transitions, and accepted results enter the existing progression engine. Duplicate and stale scenarios exercise the real rejection paths.\n\n## Alternatives considered\n\n- Random confidence/results: rejected because tests and demonstrations would be irreproducible.\n- In-memory fake store: prohibited because it bypasses persistence and audit truth.\n\n## Consequences\n\nEvery scenario is repeatable. The expected mock outcome is labeled separately from internal failures.\n\n## Migration implications\n\nThe mock adapter can be disabled or removed after later real adapters pass the same contract suite.\n\n## Security implications\n\nMock execution is server-flagged and production-disabled by default. It grants no generic progression command.\n\n## Compatibility implications\n\nResults use the same protocol, attempt state, and story event contracts as future inference.\n\r\n# ADR 0008: Typed feature flags\n\nStatus: accepted for Phase B-1\n\n## Context\n\nLater Phase B capabilities must remain hidden and unauthorized while B-1 mock surfaces are available in development and test.\n\n## Decision\n\nDefine all Vision flags in one typed registry with documented environment defaults. Server modules enforce feature availability and permissions. A serializable public subset controls presentation and adapter selection but cannot grant server access.\n\n## Alternatives considered\n\n- Local-storage flags: rejected because they are user-modifiable and unaudited.\n- Scattered environment checks: rejected because defaults and diagnostics would drift.\n\n## Consequences\n\nFlags appear in diagnostics and have enabled/disabled tests. Production defaults keep unfinished capture, build, shadow, automatic, and live AR features off.\n\n## Migration implications\n\nFlags can later move to a persistent deployment service while preserving names and types.\n\n## Security implications\n\nChanging client state cannot bypass server authorization or production mock restrictions.\n\n## Compatibility implications\n\nUnknown environment values fail to documented safe defaults.\n\r\n# ADR 0009: Verification event idempotency and stale protection\n\nStatus: accepted for Phase B-1\n\n## Context\n\nRetries, reconnects, delayed results, and duplicate delivery must not advance a story twice or complete a stale stage.\n\n## Decision\n\nGive every attempt a stable unique idempotency key derived from session, block, waypoint version, attempt, and event type. Immediately before delivery, recheck the active session, block, pinned story version, waypoint version, request state, and cancellation state. Route accepted results through existing unique `TaleVerificationEvent` and `TaleSessionEvent` keys. Persist duplicate/stale rejection metadata on the attempt.\n\n## Alternatives considered\n\n- Client-side deduplication: rejected because clients can retry, reconnect, or be duplicated.\n- Marking the attempt complete before story delivery: rejected because partial failure would be ambiguous.\n\n## Consequences\n\nDuplicate replay returns the prior outcome, creates no second progression history, and remains observable. Stale results close without delivery.\n\n## Migration implications\n\nExisting story idempotency remains unchanged; Vision attempts add another durable correlation layer.\n\n## Security implications\n\nReplayed or cross-stage results cannot unlock content.\n\n## Compatibility implications\n\nFuture adapters must preserve attempt and message identity across retries.\n\r\n", "type": "input_text"}]

allowed to pair.\");\r\n    assertExactKeys(input, [\"protocolVersion\", \"clientInstanceId\", \"publicKeyJwk\", \"accountHint\"], \"pairing request\");\r\n    if (input.protocolVersion !== CAPTURE_PROTOCOL_VERSION)\r\n      throw captureError(\"PROTOCOL_INCOMPATIBLE\", \"Browser and Companion protocol versions do not match.\");\r\n    requireIdentifier(input.clientInstanceId, this.pendingLifetimeMs).toISOString();\r\n    this.pending.set(pairingId, {\r\n      pairingId,\r\n      allowedOrigin: origin,\r\n      clientInstanceId: input.clientInstanceId,\r\n      accountHint:    allowedOrigin: pending.allowedOrigin,\r\n      clientInstanceId: pending.clientInstanceId,\r\n      accountHint: pending.accountHint,\r\n      pairingCode: pending.code,\r\n      desktopApproved: this.#expirePending();\r\n    const pending = this.pending.get(pairingId);\r\n    if (!pending) throw captureError(\"PAIRING_EXPIRED\", \"Pairing request expired.\");\r\n    if (!approved) {\r\n      this.pending.delete(pairingId);\r\n      return { pairingId, approved: false, rejected: true };\r\n    }\r\n    pending.desktopApproved = true;\r\n    pending.approvedAt = new pairing.lastSequence)\r\n      throw captureError(\"PAIRING_REPLAY_REJECTED\", \"Pairing request sequence was replayed or out of order.\");\r\n    if (pairing.requestIds.has(requestId))\r\n      throw > 500) pairing.requestIds.delete(pairing.requestIds.values().next().value);\r\n    await this.#persist();\r\n  }\r\n\r\n  listPairings() {\r\n    return [...this.pairings.values()].map((pairing) => this.frames = [];\n    this.bytes = 0;\n    this.droppedFrames = 0;\n    this.lastSequence = -1;\n    if (!Number.isInteger(this.maxFrames) || this.maxFrames < 1 || this.maxFrames > 600)\n      throw strict\";\n\nconst QUALITY_ALGORITHM_VERSION = \"b2-quality-1\";\nconst BEST_FRAME_ALGORITHM_VERSION = \"b2-temporal-diversity-1\";\n\nfunction hammingHex(left, right) {\n  if (!left || !right || left.length !== right.length) return 64;\n  let distance = 0;\n  for (let index = 0; index < left.length; index += 1) {\n    let value = Number.parseInt(left[index], 16) ^ Number.parseInt(right[index], 16);\n    while (value) {\n      distance += value & 1;\n      value >>>= 1;\n    }\n  }\n  return distance;\n}\n\nfunction perceptualHash(luminance, width, height) {\n  const bits = [];\n  for (let row = 0; row < 8; row += 1) {\n    const y = Math.min(height - 1, Math.floor(((row + 0.5) * height) / 8));\n    for (let column = 0; column < 8; column += 1) {\n luminance[y * width + nextX] ? 1 : 0);\n    }\n  }\n  let result = \"\";\n  for (let index = 0; index < bits.length; index += 4)\n    result += Number.parseInt(bits.slice(index, index + 4).join(\"\"), 2).toString(16);\n  return result.padEnd(16, \"0\");\n}\n\nfunction analyzeFrame(input, previousFrame) {\n  const { pixels, width, height } = input;\n  if (\n    !Buffer.isBuffer(pixels) ||\n    !Number.isInteger(width) ||\n    !Number.isInteger(height) ||\n    pixels.length < width * height * 4\n  )\n    throw new Error(\"CAPTURE_FRAME_INVALID\");\n  const pixelCount = width * height;\n  const luminance = Buffer.allocUnsafe(pixelCount);\n  const histogram = new Uint32Array(16);\n  let sum = 0;\n  let sumSquares = 0;\n  let dark = 0;\n  let bright = 0;\n  let black = 0;\n  for (let index = 0, pixelIndex = 0; pixelIndex < pixelCount; index += 4, pixelIndex += 1) {\n    const value = Math.round(pixels[index] * 0.2126 + pixels[index + 1] * 0.7152 + pixels[index + 2] * 0.0722);\n    luminance[pixelIndex] = value;\n    histogram[Math.min(15, value >>> 4)] += 1;\n    sum += value;\n    sumSquares += value * value;\n    if (value <= 12) black += 1;\n    if (value <= 24) dark += 1;\n    if (value >= 232) bright += 1;\n  }\n  const mean = sum / pixelCount;\n  const variance = Math.max(0, sumSquares / pixelCount - mean * mean);\n  let entropy = 0;\n  for (const count of histogram) {\n    if (!count) continue;\n    const probability = count / pixelCount;\n    entropy -= probability * Math.log2(probability);\n  }\n  let edge = 0;\n  let edgeSamples = 0;\n  const step = Math.max(1, Math.floor(Math.min(width, height) / 180));\n  for (let y = step; y < height; y += step) {\n    for (let x = step; x < width; x += step) {\n      const current = luminance[y * width + x];\n      edge += Math.abs(current - luminance[y * width + x - step]);\n      edge += Math.abs(current - luminance[(y - step) * width + x]);\n      edgeSamples += 2;\n    }\n  }\n  let motion = null;\n  if (previousFrame?.luminance?.length === luminance.length) {\n    let difference = 0;\n    let samples = 0;\n    for (let index = 0; index < luminance.length; index += Math.max(1, Math.floor(luminance.length / 4096))) {\n      difference += Math.abs(luminance[index] - previousFrame.luminance[index]);\n      samples += 1;\n    }\n    motion = difference / Math.max(1, samples) / 255;\n  }\n  const hash = perceptualHash(luminance, width, height);\n  const duplicateDistance = previousFrame?.quality?.perceptualHash\n    ? hammingHex(hash, previousFrame.quality.perceptualHash)\n    : null;\n  const sharpness = Math.min(1, edge / Math.max(1, edgeSamples) / 32);\n  const reasons = [];\n  if (black / pixelCount > 0.85) reasons.push(\"FRAME_MOSTLY_BLACK\");\n  if (mean < 28) reasons.push(\"FRAME_LOW_INFORMATION\");\n  if (duplicateDistance !== null && duplicateDistance <= 2) reasons.push(\"FRAME_NEAR_DUPLICATE\");\n  if (motion !== null && motion > 0.32) luminanceVariance: variance / (255 * 255),\n      darkClippingRatio: dark / pixelCount,\n      brightClippingRatio: bright / pixelCount,\n      blackFrameRatio: black / pixelCount,\n      contrast: Math.min(1, Math.sqrt(variance) / 64),\n      entropy: entropy / 4,\n      perceptualHash: hash,\n      duplicateDistance,\n      nearDuplicate: duplicateDistance !== null && duplicateDistance <= 2,\n      motion,\n      reasons,\n      usable: reasons.every(\n        (reason) => ![\"FRAME_MOSTLY_BLACK\", \"FRAME_BLURRY\", \"FRAME_EXCESSIVE_MOTION\"].includes(reason),\n      ),\n    },\n  };\n}\n\nfunction selectBestFrames(frames, options = {}) {\n  const maximum = options.maximum ?? 12;\n  const minimum = options.minimum ?? 6;\n  const usable = frames.filter((frame) => frame.quality.usable);\n  const selected = [];\n  if (usable.length) {\n    const bucketCount = Math.min(maximum, usable.length);\n    for (let bucket = 0; bucket < bucketCount; bucket += 1) {\n      const start = Math.floor((bucket * usable.length) / bucketCount);\n      const end = Math.max(start + 1, Math.floor(((bucket + 1) * usable.length) / bucketCount));\n      const candidates = usable.slice(start, end).sort((left, right) => {\n        const score = (frame) =>\n          frame.quality.sharpness * 0.45 +\n          frame.quality.contrast * 0.2 +\n          frame.quality.entropy * 0.15 +\n          Math.min(0.2, (frame.quality.motion ?? 0.08) * 0.8);\n        return score(right) - score(left) || left.sequence - right.sequence;\n      });\n      const diverse = candidates.find(\n        (candidate) =>\n          !selected.some(\n            (existing) => hammingHex(existing.quality.perceptualHash, candidate.quality.perceptualHash) <= 3,\n          ),\n      );\n      if (diverse) selected.push(diverse);\n    }\n  }\n  selected.sort((left, right) => left.capturedAtMs - right.capturedAtMs || left.sequence - right.sequence);\n  const reasons = };\n}\n\nfunction average(values) {\n  const finite = values.filter((value) => Number.isFinite(value));\n  return finite.length ? finite.reduce((sum, value) => sum + value, 0) / finite.length : [{"text": "Script completed\nWall time 0.4 seconds\nOutput:\n", "type": "input_text"}, {"text": "Exit code: 0\nWall time: 0.3 seconds\nOutput:\n# ADR 0011: Electron window capture and one Companion coordinator\n\nStatus: accepted for Phase B-2\n\n## Context\n\nB-1 selected Electron because the shared application requires a dynamic Next.js/Prisma server and the host had no Rust toolchain. B-2 requires real user-selected Windows application-window capture for both the integrated desktop and a paired browser without duplicating capture code or moving native logic into React.\n\nElectron exposes Windows application windows through main-process `desktopCapturer` sources and captures an approved source through Chromium media APIs. A source ID contains the HWND on Windows. This is a supported, read-only individual-window capture path and does not modify the source application.\n\n## Decision\n\nCreate one `CompanionCoordinator` and one `CaptureCore` in the Electron main process. A dedicated hidden, sandboxed capture worker owns the media stream and MediaRecorder. It receives only a selected `window:*` source ID. It sends downscaled binary frame buffers and bounded recording chunks to the coordinator.\n\nDesktop IPC and browser WebSocket adapters call the same coordinator commands. Target enumeration and selection occur in the main process and return sanitized candidate metadata plus small thumbnails only after an explicit user action. The app never selects a likely Sea of Thieves source silently and never offers full-display capture by default.\n\nThe capability report names the API `ELECTRON_DESKTOP_CAPTURER`. It does not assert that a particular internal Chromium capture backend is active.\n\n## Alternatives considered\n\n- Tauri/Rust Windows Graphics Capture: rejected because Rust is absent and B-1 already chose Electron for the same shared application.\n- A new C# Windows service: rejected because no .NET SDK is installed and it would add a second build, update, and signing boundary.\n- Capture in the shared React component: rejected because it would mix UI, platform, lifecycle, privacy, and resource ownership.\n- Separate desktop and browser capture implementations: prohibited because behavior and security would drift.\n- Full-display capture fallback: rejected because it expands privacy scope beyond the selected game window.\n\n## Consequences\n\nCapture has one lifecycle, quality pipeline, ring buffer, storage policy, error catalog, and test harness. Electron remains the local Companion process. A hidden renderer/GPU process can fail without corrupting Studio persistence; the coordinator detects loss, clears transient frames, and requires a safe restart.\n\n## Security implications\n\nThe worker is sandboxed, has no Node integration, and accepts commands only from the coordinator. UI renderers cannot send worker events. Source IDs are validated as Windows window IDs and checked against the current enumerated candidate set. No arbitrary media, filesystem, process, or display command is exposed.\n\n## Compatibility implications\n\nThe architecture is Windows-only for B-2. Future capture backends may implement the same `CaptureWorker` and `TargetProvider` interfaces without changing shared UI or protocol contracts.\n\r\n# ADR 0012: Challenge-authenticated loopback Companion pairing\n\nStatus: accepted for Phase B-2\n\n## Context\n\nBrowser/PWA surfaces need the same local capture core as the desktop application. A generic localhost API would let unrelated websites probe or operate capture. Browsers cannot add an Authorization header during the WebSocket upgrade, and putting a bearer token in the URL would leak it into logs and diagnostics.\n\n## Decision\n\nBind an HTTP/WebSocket service only to `127.0.0.1`. Accept only exact configured origins. Pairing is an explicit two-surface ceremony:\n\n1. an allowed browser origin creates a short-lived pending request;\n   the browser includes a newly generated ECDSA P-256 public key;\n2. the desktop Companion displays the origin and a random code;\n3. the user enters that code in the browser;\n4. the Companion returns an origin-bound, expiring pairing ID;\n5. the WebSocket sends a fresh challenge;\n6. the browser proves possession by signing the challenge, pairing ID, origin, and protocol with ECDSA P-256/SHA-256;\n7. every command then uses a unique request ID and strictly increasing sequence.\n\nPersist only the public key, expiration, approved origin, device identity, bounded replay metadata, and revocation state. Keep the private key in browser session memory only. Reject used challenges, invalid signatures, duplicate request IDs, non-increasing sequences, stale sessions, incompatible protocols, oversized messages, disallowed origins, and rate-limit violations.\n\nDesktop integration bypasses browser pairing but still uses the same protocol schema and coordinator allowlist through private IPC.\n\n## Alternatives considered\n\n- Wildcard CORS or unauthenticated localhost: prohibited.\n- Bearer token in WebSocket URL: rejected because URLs are routinely logged.\n- Long-lived pairing code: rejected because it is replayable and brute-forceable.\n- Automatic origin approval: rejected because capture must not begin without visible user awareness.\n- Remote/LAN binding: outside B-2 and requires a separate threat model.\n\n## Consequences\n\nPairing can expire and be revoked without restarting the Companion. A captured authentication proof cannot be replayed on a new connection because the challenge changes. The Companion stores no symmetric pairing secret. Loss of the browser's in-memory private key requires a new explicit pairing ceremony.\n\n## Security implications\n\nThe browser protocol exposes typed capture operations, managed artifact preview/delete, status, privacy, and diagnostics only. It exposes no arbitrary file path, command execution, shell, full-resolution frame stream, or unrestricted preview endpoint.\n\n## Compatibility implications\n\nCapture protocol 2.0 is negotiated explicitly. B-1 protocol 1.0 remains intact for its deterministic development verifier and is not silently upgraded.\n\r\n# ADR 0013: Scoped Windows hotkey and selected-window health monitor\n\nStatus: accepted for Phase B-2\n\n## Context\n\nElectron's `globalShortcut` reports activation and registration conflict but does not expose key release. B-2 requires press-and-hold initiation, release-to-finalize, repeat suppression, conflict reporting, and selected-window minimize/close/resize health. The Windows capture source ID includes the HWND, but Electron does not expose `IsIconic` or the target client rectangle.\n\nThe audited host has PowerShell 5.1 and .NET Framework compilation support but no Rust, C++, or .NET SDK.\n\n## Decision\n\nShip a fixed PowerShell sidecar that compiles one source-controlled C# Win32 interop surface in memory with `Add-Type`. It uses:\n\n- `RegisterHotKey` with `MOD_NOREPEAT` to detect conflicts;\n- `GetAsyncKeyState` to poll only the configured trigger key and required modifiers for down/up state;\n- `IsWindow`, `IsIconic`, and `GetClientRect` for the selected HWND;\n- a message loop and bounded health heartbeat;\n- newline-delimited, fixed-shape JSON over standard output.\n\nThe Electron coordinator launches it hidden with a fixed script path and validated numeric arguments. There is no generic script, command, or process-launch API. The monitor emits no typed text, scan code, full window title, or unrelated key event.\n\nThe helper itself owns conflict detection so registration and release observation use one authority. When the hotkey is disabled, the helper restarts in health-only mode for the currently selected HWND. The UI also provides a local mouse/keyboard hold button and toggle accessibility mode.\n\n## Alternatives considered\n\n- Electron `globalShortcut` only: rejected because release cannot end the scan.\n- Polling all keyboard state from JavaScript: rejected because Electron exposes no safe global key-state API. The fixed monitor polls only the chosen preset.\n- Native npm keyboard-hook dependency: rejected because it adds ABI-specific binaries and rebuild/signing risk to Electron 41.\n- Input injection or game binding: prohibited.\n- Logging the full keyboard stream: prohibited and unnecessary.\n\n## Consequences\n\nThe monitor is Windows-only and may be blocked by local application-control policy. Such a block is a truthful `HOTKEY_UNAVAILABLE` state; it does not disable the in-application control. Hotkey disable unregisters the binding while preserving selected-window health monitoring; Companion shutdown or app exit terminates the helper. A maximum scan duration and coordinator cleanup cover lost release events.\n\n## Security implications\n\nThe monitor has no administrator requirement, does not attach to the game, does not inject a DLL, and does not synthesize, suppress, forward, or log input. Only an allowlisted preset's modifier/key combination is accepted by the coordinator. Compatibility with a game's own binding for the same reserved global combination remains a manual test item.\n\n## Compatibility implications\n\nFuture signed native helpers may replace the script behind the same `HotkeyService` and `TargetHealthProvider` interfaces. Public distribution still requires signing and reputation testing in Phase B-6.\n\r\n# Phase B-2 Native Companion Architecture\n\nApplication version: `0.4.0-b2`  \nCapture protocol: `2.0`  \nRecording manifest: `1`  \nEvidence metadata: `1`\n\n## Product boundary\n\nPhase B-2 extends the B-1 Electron shell and shared Next.js application. It does not create a second product or a browser-owned capture implementation.\n\n```text\nShared /vision-companion React surface\n  -> DesktopCapturePlatformAdapter -> restricted context-isolated IPC ---+\n  -> WebCapturePlatformAdapter -> paired loopback WebSocket -------------+\n                                                                       CompanionCoordinator\n                                                                         -> one CaptureCore\n                                                                            -> ElectronTargetProvider\n                                                                            -> sandboxed CaptureWorker\n                                                                            -> bounded quality/ring pipeline\n                                                                            -> CompanionStorage\n                                                                            -> Windows health/hotkey monitor\n```\n\nThe React layer gathers user intent and renders state. It does not own media streams, files, state transitions, quality algorithms, pairing authorization, or retention behavior.\n\n## Process boundaries\n\n| Boundary                | Responsibility                                                                                      | Explicitly unavailable                                                  |\n| ----------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------- |\n| Shared Next renderer    | Status, explicit target confirmation, creator/player controls, pairing ceremony, retention controls | Node, shell, arbitrary IPC, raw native frames                           |\n| Electron main           | One coordinator, sender/origin validation, target enumeration, tray, loopback listener              | Game injection, memory access, input synthesis                          |\n| Hidden sandboxed worker | Approved `window:HWND:other_id` media stream, downscale, MediaRecorder                              | Node, navigation, arbitrary source selection, filesystem                |\n| Fixed PowerShell helper | Selected HWND health and one allowlisted hotkey preset                                              | Full keyboard logging, input suppression/forwarding, arbitrary commands |\n| Loopback server         | Pairing and typed protocol adaptation                                                               | LAN binding, wildcard CORS, arbitrary paths, generic execution          |\n| Next/Prisma server      | Owned draft creator-manifest persistence and audit                                                  | Player pixels, native file reads, location decision                     |\n\nThe capability name is `ELECTRON_DESKTOP_CAPTURER`. Chromium may select a supported Windows backend internally; B-2 does not claim a particular backend as an application guarantee.\n\n## Capture state machine\n\nThe allowed states are `IDLE`, `PAIRING`, `READY`, `TARGET_SELECTION_REQUIRED`, `TARGET_SELECTED`, `STARTING`, `CAPTURING`, `PAUSED`, `FINALIZING`, `PROCESSING_CAPTURE`, `COMPLETED`, `CANCELLED`, `FAILED`, and `TARGET_LOST`.\n\nEvery transition is validated, sequenced, timestamped, correlated to a session where applicable, emitted as an event, and written to structured logs. Duplicate stop returns the prior metadata-only completion for the same session. Stale session IDs are rejected. A minimized or closed target becomes `TARGET_LOST`; restore can return a retained valid target to `TARGET_SELECTED`. A closed HWND invalidates the target.\n\n## Target semantics\n\n- Only `desktopCapturer.getSources({types: [\"window\"]})` candidates are accepted.\n- The user explicitly confirms a current enumerated source; a likely Sea of Thieves label is convenience only.\n- Full display capture is not offered.\n- Candidate titles are sanitized and bounded. Ordinary logs never receive the title.\n- Small selection thumbnails are capped; native frames are not serialized as JSON.\n- B-2 targets are process-session-only. `remember: true` is rejected, and the target expires on Companion exit or invalid HWND.\n- The HWND helper reports client size, minimized/restored state, and closure every 500 ms while a target exists, even when the global hotkey is disabled.\n\n## Frame and queue architecture\n\nThe worker samples a native-size selected-window stream into `320x180` RGBA analysis frames. Electron IPC transfers binary typed arrays. Player mode inserts them into a deterministic oldest-first ring with both a frame ceiling and a 32 MiB byte ceiling. The default is 5 seconds at 10 samples/second; the governed range is 3-8 seconds and 8-12 samples/second. The ring can retain at most 84 frames.\n\nQuality processing derives luminance, clipping, contrast, entropy, sharpness proxy, perceptual hash, near-duplicate distance, and adjacent-frame motion. Selection uses temporal buckets and perceptual diversity, preserves chronology, and returns at most 12 frame references. Continuous duplicates produce a frozen-stream result.\n\nThe B-2 capture-only consumer completes before `BoundedFrameRing.clear()` zero-fills pixel and luminance buffers. No raw player frame is written to disk, sent to the Next server, returned in protocol JSON, or retained after completion/cancel/error/shutdown.\n\nCreator mode uses the same stream and quality path. MediaRecorder WebM chunks are drained in order into an app-managed `.part` file, capped at 2 GiB. Stop waits for asynchronous final MediaRecorder data before hashing/finalization. The completed artifact and sidecar use generated IDs; cancellation and failure remove the temporary file.\n\n## Initial performance budgets\n\n| Resource                   | Budget                                             |\n| -------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------- |\n| Player raw-frame memory    | 32 MiB hard byte ceiling                           |\n| Player ring                | 84 frames maximum                                  |\n| Player duration            | 3-8 seconds; 5-second default                      |\n| Analysis rate              | 8-12 FPS; 10 FPS default                           |\n| Evidence selection         | 3-12 metadata frame references; normal target 6-12 |\n| Creator media              | 2 GiB hard ceiling; 10-minute command ceiling      |\n| Pairing request body       | 32 KiB                                             |\n| Incoming WebSocket message | 64 KiB                                             |\n| Target candidates          | 64 maximum; bounded thumbnails/icons               |\n| Authentication             | 10-second socket proof timeout                     |\n| Command response           | 20-second browser adapter timeout                  |\n\nThe deterministic Electron harness measured five repeated scans with no orphan `.part` files, no active recording/worker session, and a 10,425,975-byte external-memory delta in the final recorded run. This is a harness measurement, not a Sea of Thieves gameplay-stutter claim.\n\n## Capability and degradation model\n\nCapabilities report OS/CPU/memory, Electron GPU devices, encoder candidates, hardware-acceleration observation, CPU metadata fallback, protocol/package versions, storage category/free bytes, modes, resolutions, preview behavior, hotkey support, and privacy budgets. They explicitly report `localInference: false`, `locationVerification: false`, and `cloudBuild: false`.\n\nExclusive-fullscreen reliability is not claimed. If the selected source stops, closes, minimizes, or freezes, B-2 returns a capture error or insufficient-capture result and recommends restore or Borderless Windowed. It never uses injection as a fallback.\n\n## B-1 compatibility seam\n\nThe historical deterministic B-1 verifier remains available only as a development/test consumer. Its result endpoint is gated by `mock_verification_consumer`, which defaults off in production, and packaged Electron rejects legacy mock preparation. B-2 capture results never become B-1 verification results implicitly.\n\r\n# Phase B-2 Capture Protocol 2.0\n\n## Envelope\n\nBoth adapters use the same logical contract. Desktop IPC supplies a command plus validated payload directly; browser transport uses this strict envelope:\n\n```json\n{\n  \"protocolVersion\": \"2.0\",\n  \"messageType\": \"capture.command\",\n  \"messageId\": \"message_...\",\n  \"requestId\": \"request_...\",\n  \"sessionId\": \"pairing_...\",\n  \"timestamp\": \"2026-07-18T07:30:00.000Z\",\n  \"sequence\": 1,\n  \"payload\": {\n    \"command\": \"capture.scan.start\",\n    \"input\": {\n      \"requestId\": \"request_player_scan\",\n      \"attemptId\": \"attempt_player_scan\",\n      \"durationMs\": 5000,\n      \"sampleFps\": 10,\n      \"minimumFrames\": 6\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\nUnknown envelope and command fields are rejected. Browser sequences must increase, request IDs cannot repeat, and the pairing origin/protocol must match.\n\n## Operations\n\n| Group                          | Commands                                                                                         |\n| ------------------------------ | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ |\n| Capability/status              | `capture.getCapabilities`, `capture.getStatus`                                                   |\n| Target                         | `capture.listTargets`, `capture.selectTarget`                                                    |\n| Creator                        | `capture.creator.start`, `.pause`, `.resume`, `.stop`, `.cancel`, `.list`, `.preview`, `.delete` |\n| Player                         | `capture.scan.start`, `.stop`, `.cancel`                                                         |\n| Privacy                        | `capture.privacy.pause`, `.resume`                                                               |\n| Desktop hotkey                 | `capture.hotkey.configure`, `.disable`                                                           |\n| Desktop pairing administration | `capture.pairing.pending`, `.approve`, `.list`, `.revoke`                                        |\n| Diagnostics                    | `capture.diagnostic.create`, `.export`                                                           |\n\nThe browser allowlist omits hotkey configuration and pairing administration. Preview and diagnostic export return short-lived, exact-origin token URLs to one managed artifact; they never accept a path.\n\n## Events\n\nAuthenticated browser clients and the desktop renderer receive `status`, `state`, `capture-progress`, `capture-completed`, and `capture-error`. A fresh WebSocket first receives `companion.challenge` and cannot send capture commands before successful authentication.\n\n## Pairing proof\n\n1. Browser generates an ECDSA P-256 key pair and sends only the public JWK with an allowed exact origin.\n2. Desktop shows that origin and a random six-digit, two-minute code.\n3. User approves in desktop and enters the code in the browser.\n4. The pairing is origin-bound, expires after 30 minutes, and persists only public/replay metadata.\n5. WebSocket sends a 256-bit random challenge.\n6. Browser signs `challenge|pairingId|origin|2.0` with ECDSA P-256/SHA-256.\n7. Revocation closes matching sockets; expiration, signature failure, reused challenge, duplicate request ID, or non-increasing sequence is rejected.\n\nNo pairing secret, code, signature, cookie, or private key is logged or stored by the Companion.\n\n## Capture-only result\n\nThe only B-2 result values are:\n\n- `EVIDENCE_CAPTURED`\n- `INSUFFICIENT_CAPTURE_EVIDENCE`\n- `CAPTURE_CANCELLED`\n- `CAPTURE_ERROR`\n\nRepresentative player completion:\n\n```json\n{\n  \"sessionId\": \"scan_...\",\n  \"result\": \"EVIDENCE_CAPTURED\",\n  \"reasons\": [],\n  \"captureOnly\": true,\n  \"verificationResult\": null,\n  \"evidenceBundle\": {\n    \"schemaVersion\": 1,\n    \"protocolVersion\": \"2.0\",\n    \"captureApi\": \"ELECTRON_DESKTOP_CAPTURER\",\n    \"selection\": {\n      \"algorithmVersion\": \"b2-temporal-diversity-1\",\n      \"selectedFrameCount\": 7,\n      \"frames\": [{ \"frameRef\": \"frame_scan_..._3\", \"sequence\": 3, \"capturedAtMs\": 0, \"width\": 320, \"height\": 180 }]\n    },\n    \"retention\": {\n      \"rawFramesWrittenToDisk\": false,\n      \"transientFramesCleared\": true,\n      \"replayable\": false\n    },\n    \"verification\": { \"performed\": false, \"outcome\": null }\n  }\n}\n```\n\nFrame references are metadata receipts, not arbitrary frame-download handles.\n\n## Error catalog\n\nErrors contain `code`, bounded developer message, user title/message, recommended action, retry/reselection flags, and diagnostic availability.\n\n| Area                       | Codes                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        |\n| -------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |\n| Target/stream              | `CAPTURE_SOURCE_NOT_SELECTED`, `CAPTURE_SOURCE_CLOSED`, `CAPTURE_SOURCE_MINIMIZED`, `CAPTURE_SOURCE_UNAVAILABLE`, `CAPTURE_PERMISSION_DENIED`, `CAPTURE_FORMAT_CHANGED`, `CAPTURE_FRAME_TIMEOUT`                                             |\n| Quality/resource           | `CAPTURE_INSUFFICIENT_FRAMES`, `CAPTURE_EXCESSIVE_BLUR`, `CAPTURE_EXCESSIVE_DUPLICATES`, `CAPTURE_EXCESSIVE_MOTION`, `CAPTURE_INSUFFICIENT_MOTION`, `CAPTURE_STORAGE_UNAVAILABLE`                                                            |\n| Lifecycle/privacy          | `CAPTURE_ALREADY_ACTIVE`, `CAPTURE_NOT_ACTIVE`, `CAPTURE_PRIVACY_PAUSED`, `CAPTURE_REQUEST_STALE`                                                                                                                                            |\n| Pairing/transport          | `PAIRING_REQUIRED`, `PAIRING_EXPIRED`, `PAIRING_REVOKED`, `PAIRING_CODE_INVALID`, `PAIRING_REPLAY_REJECTED`, `ORIGIN_NOT_ALLOWED`, `PROTOCOL_INCOMPATIBLE`, `COMPANION_UNAVAILABLE`, `COMPANION_RATE_LIMITED`, `COMPANION_PAYLOAD_TOO_LARGE` |\n| Hotkey/diagnostic/artifact | `HOTKEY_CONFLICT`, `HOTKEY_UNAVAILABLE`, `HOTKEY_RELEASE_LOST`, `DIAGNOSTIC_CONSENT_REQUIRED`, `ARTIFACT_NOT_FOUND`, `ARTIFACT_PATH_INVALID`                                                                                                 |\n| Boundary                   | `VALIDATION_FAILED`, `INTERNAL_ERROR`                                                                                                                                                                                                        |\n\nSystem or capture failures never become `NOT_AT_TARGET` or `VERIFIED`.\n\r\n", "type": B-2 will therefore use Electron's supported capture API and a narrowly scoped PowerShell/Win32 monitor for the two capabilities Electron does not expose: selected HWND health and key-up notification.\n\n## Transport audit and decision\n\nThe existing desktop path is authenticated by the Electron process boundary and a fixed preload allowlist. B-2 keeps that path and routes every command to one `CaptureCore` instance.\n\nThe browser path will use a second adapter over a loopback-only WebSocket service owned by the same Companion coordinator:\n\n- bind only to `127.0.0.1`;\n- exact configured origin allowlist, never wildcard CORS;\n- explicit short-lived pairing request visible in desktop UI;\n- user-entered pairing code;\n- persisted public keys only; browser private keys remain in session memory;\n- per-connection challenge authentication;\n- expiring session, revocation, request IDs, monotonic sequence, replay cache, rate limits, and payload limits;\n- protocol negotiation before capture commands;\n- no generic command, path, or full-resolution-frame endpoint.\n\nDesktop IPC and browser WebSocket messages share protocol 2.0 and the same command handlers. Protocol 1.0 remains available to the existing B-1 mock flow; B-2 capture does not silently reinterpret B-1 verification results.\n\n## Native process and resource boundary\n\n```text\nshared Next.js UI\n  -> DesktopCaptureAdapter -> restricted Electron IPC ----+\n  -> WebCompanionAdapter -> paired loopback WebSocket ----+--> CompanionCoordinator\n                                                            -> one CaptureCore\n                                                               -> TargetProvider\n                                                               -> hidden sandboxed capture worker\n                                                               -> bounded frame/quality pipeline\n                                                               -> creator artifact store\n                                                               -> evidence/diagnostic services\n                                                               -> scoped Win32 health/hotkey monitor\n```\n\nThe hidden capture worker receives only an approved source ID and capture configuration. It returns downscaled pixel buffers and bounded WebM chunks over binary Electron IPC. Full frames do not travel through JSON. Player frames never use disk. Creator files are streamed only into the managed per-user artifact directory.\n\n## Safety boundary\n\nB-2 will not:\n\n- inject into Sea of Thieves or any other process;\n- read game memory, files, network traffic, or account data;\n- synthesize, suppress, or forward keyboard/mouse/controller input;\n- create an in-game overlay;\n- silently choose a window;\n- capture an entire display by default;\n- upload raw frames;\n- return `VERIFIED` or label a capture failure as a wrong location.\n\nThe key monitor observes only the configured key and required modifier state, emits only press/release state, records no text, never suppresses input, and shuts down with the Companion. Registration failure is surfaced as `HOTKEY_CONFLICT`; the in-application hold/toggle control remains available.\n\n## Preflight conclusion\n\nThe B-1 architecture can support B-2 without a second frontend or duplicate capture implementation. The selected architecture is implementable on the audited host, packages with the existing Electron runtime, preserves the strict native-command boundary, and provides honest degradation when real game/display conditions cannot be captured. ADRs 0011 through 0013 record the material decisions before implementation begins.\n\r\n# Phase B-2 Storage and Database Changes\n\n## Local Companion storage\n\nThe root is derived from Electron `app.getPath(\"userData\")`; no user or machine path is hard-coded. `CompanionStorage` owns:\n\n```text\ncompanion/\n  configuration/\n  pairings/pairings-v2.json\n  recordings/creator/artifact_<uuid>.webm\n  recordings/creator/artifact_<uuid>.manifest.json\n  diagnostics/diagnostic_<uuid>.json.gz\n  logs/companion.jsonl\n  temporary/artifact_<uuid>.part\n```\n\nCreator physical names use generated IDs. The manifest stores schema/protocol/core versions, target metadata, purpose/label, native and normalized dimensions, timestamps, duration/rate/count, quality/interruption summaries, encoding, file size, SHA-256, and retention authorization. Stop atomically moves media and manifest into the creator directory; failure removes partial finalization. Preview and deletion accept only generated artifact IDs.\n\nPairings persist public JWKs, exact origins, expiration/revocation, last sequence, and bounded request IDs. Codes, signatures, browser private keys, and symmetric secrets are absent.\n\nPlayer frames never enter this tree. Startup removes only bounded `.part`/`.tmp` files inside `temporary`; it does not recursively clear the user-data root.\n\n## Prisma changes\n\nBoth MySQL and SQLite schemas add creator-capture fields to `VisionCaptureSession` and `VisionRecordingAsset`, plus:\n\n- `VisionCaptureInterruption`\n- `VisionDiagnosticBundle`\n- `VisionCapturePreference`\n\nCreator manifest persistence validates ownership of a draft `VisionWaypointVersion`, stores `companion://creator/<artifactId>` rather than a machine path, creates interruption rows, and writes a correlated platform audit event in the same transaction. Content hash and session keys make retries idempotent. Local deletion marks the database asset deleted and writes a second audit event.\n\nMigrations:\n\n- SQLite: `prisma/migrations/20260718090000_vision_capture_b2/migration.sql`\n- MySQL 8: `prisma/mysql-migrations/0006_vision_capture_b2/migration.sql`\n\nAll changes are additive. No B-1 column or record is removed.\n\n## Retention\n\n| Data                           | Default                                                     | User action                                               |\n| ------------------------------ | ----------------------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------- |\n| Player pixel/luminance buffers | Memory only; zero-filled after consumption                  | None; cannot persist through B-2 protocol                 |\n| Player evidence metadata       | Returned to caller; not automatically stored by native core | Future consumer decides metadata persistence              |\n| Creator WebM/manifest          | Local app data until deleted                                | Preview/delete in Companion                               |\n| Creator database metadata      | Audited; deletion is a tombstone                            | Retained for explainability                               |\n| Pairing metadata               | 30-minute expiry; public key only                           | Revoke in desktop                                         |\n| Diagnostic bundle              | Local metadata-only archive                                 | Explicit create, download, remove from app-data directory |\n| Ordinary log                   | Local fixed-field JSONL                                     | Remove with Companion user data per operator policy       |\n\n## Rollback\n\n1. Disable `FEATURE_VISION_COMPANION`, `FEATURE_NATIVE_WINDOW_CAPTURE`, `FEATURE_CREATOR_CAPTURE`, `FEATURE_BROWSER_COMPANION_PAIRING`, `FEATURE_CAPTURE_PREVIEW`, and `FEATURE_DIAGNOSTIC_CAPTURE`.\n2. Stop the Electron Companion; this terminates capture, unregisters the hotkey, stops loopback, and clears transient player buffers.\n3. Deploy the B-1 application commit. Its historical mock result remains development/test-only under the B-2 safety gate unless that specific gate is also reverted deliberately.\n4. Leave additive B-2 database columns/tables in place by default. They do not alter B-1 reads and preserve audit history.\n5. Only after a verified database backup and an explicit destructive maintenance window, reverse foreign keys/indexes/tables and rebuild altered tables from the pre-B-2 schema. The repository does not automate destructive downgrade SQL.\n6. Local B-2 creator media can be removed through the app first. If uninstall cleanup is required, resolve Electron's actual user-data directory and remove only its `companion` child after preserving desired creator recordings. Never delete a broad AppData directory.\n\nGenerated `dist`, `.desktop-bundle`, validation databases, screenshots, and temporary harness directories are not source and may be regenerated.\n\r\n# Phase B-2 Security and Privacy Review\n\n## Privacy defaults\n\n- Capture is inactive until the user explicitly selects a window and starts a mode.\n- The route header, tray tooltip, and status payload visibly distinguish active, paused, and inactive states.\n- Player pixels remain in a 32 MiB in-memory ring, are consumed locally, zero-filled, and never written to disk.\n- Creator WebM persists only after an explicit creator start; the UI supports preview and confirmed deletion.\n- Diagnostic bundles are metadata-only in B-2. An include-frames request requires consent and is then rejected as unsupported rather than silently retaining frames.\n- No cloud upload exists. `allowCloudUpload` records future authorization intent only and never initiates a transfer.\n- Targets are not remembered; source IDs expire with the process or HWND.\n- The service worker treats `/vision-companion` and every API route as network-owned/no-store.\n\n## Local Companion threat review\n\n| Threat                             | Defense and test evidence                                                                                                           |\n| ---------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |\n| Malicious website requests pairing | Exact origin allowlist; no wildcard; origin shown in desktop; explicit approval/code; disallowed-origin HTTP test                   |\n| Origin reuses another pairing      | Pairing and signature bind exact origin; WebSocket upgrade checks origin                                                            |\n| Code/proof replay                  | Two-minute code, five-attempt ceiling, one-time pending request, fresh challenge, used-challenge set, sequence/request replay cache |\n| Stolen server credential           | No symmetric server secret exists; only browser in-memory private key can sign                                                      |\n| Localhost CSRF/PNA                 | Exact Origin required on every HTTP request; no credentialless origin; PNA response only for an already allowed origin              |\n| Arbitrary commands                 | Fixed desktop and browser command sets plus strict payload keys; no generic execute endpoint                                        |\n| Arbitrary files/path traversal     | Generated identifiers, managed roots, resolved-path checks, exact preview/download token records                                    |\n| Oversized/denial payload           | 32 KiB HTTP bodies, 64 KiB inbound WebSocket, rate limiter, capture-session exclusivity, bounded source list                        |\n| Protocol downgrade/malformed data  | Literal protocol 2.0 and strict runtime schemas; incompatible version errors                                                        |\n| Invisible capture                  | Explicit selected target, active status, tray indicator, UI controls, state events                                                  |\n| Raw frame exfiltration             | No frame protocol command, no frame JSON, only bounded small selection thumbnails and creator preview                               |\n| Secret leakage                     | Logger fixed-field projection; tests prove codes/secrets/pixels/titles are dropped                                                  |\n| Temporary-file leakage             | Generated `.part`, startup bounded cleanup, cancellation/failure cleanup, repeated-scan/recording tests                             |\n| Stale/revoked pairing              | Expiry checks on use; This record must not be represented as game-specific performance certification.\n\r\n# Phase B-2 User and Developer Troubleshooting\n\n## Start the development Companion\n\n```powershell\ncd C:\\path\\to\\the\\repository\nnpm ci\nnpm run db:generate\nnpm run db:migrate\nnpm run desktop:dev\n```\n\nOpen **Navigate > Vision Companion**. Use the actual repository path on the current machine; no source file contains the example path above.\n\n## Window does not appear\n\n- Make sure the application owns a normal visible Windows window and is not minimized.\n- Press **Select Game Window** again; B-2 never selects by process/title silently.\n- Prefer Sea of Thieves Borderless Windowed if exclusive fullscreen is absent or frozen.\n- If the game restarted, the old HWND is invalid; select the replacement explicitly.\n- A target is intentionally not remembered across Companion restarts.\n\n## Minimized, closed, frozen, or black\n\n- `CAPTURE_SOURCE_MINIMIZED`: restore the selected window. The retained valid HWND should return to selected state.\n- `CAPTURE_SOURCE_CLOSED`: reopen and reselect; closure invalidates the target.\n- `CAPTURE_FRAME_TIMEOUT` or frozen/duplicate warning: restore, expose changing content, use Borderless Windowed, and retry.\n- Mostly black/dark/bright/blurred: change the scene or sweep more slowly. These are capture-quality messages, not a claim that the location is wrong.\n\n## Hotkey fails\n\n- `HOTKEY_CONFLICT` means another application already registered that combination. Choose another preset or use the in-app pointer/Space/Enter control.\n- Application-control policy may block the fixed PowerShell helper; use the in-app control and collect a metadata diagnostic.\n- Disable removes the registration but selected-window health monitoring remains active.\n- Do not use an input-injection tool to test release; press and release the configured physical key.\n\n## Browser cannot pair\n\n- The desktop Companion must be running locally and listening on `127.0.0.1:32179`.\n- Request pairing, approve the exact displayed origin in desktop, then enter the displayed six-digit code before two minutes.\n- Refresh loses the in-memory browser private key by design; request a new pairing.\n- Expired/revoked pairing requires a new ceremony.\n- For nonstandard development/hosted origins, add the exact origin to `TALL_TALE_COMPANION_ALLOWED_ORIGINS`; never use `*`.\n- Keep `NEXT_PUBLIC_COMPANION_URL` on approved `127.0.0.1` or `localhost`; CSP rejects non-loopback values.\n- Browser private-network or mixed-content policies may differ for an HTTPS deployment. Validate the intended production origin/browser before release; do not weaken CORS or bind to LAN as a workaround.\n\n## Creator recording fails\n\n- Check free disk in capabilities and app-data permissions.\n- The hard local file ceiling is 2 GiB and the command duration ceiling is 10 minutes.\n- Stop waits for final encoder chunks. If the encoder/source fails, the `.part` file is removed or cleaned at next startup.\n- Creator manifest server persistence additionally requires a signed-in creator, CSRF, ownership, and a draft waypoint version ID. The local recording remains available if database persistence fails.\n\n## Diagnostics\n\nCreate **metadata-only diagnostic bundle**, then prepare and download its one-time five-minute link. It includes versions, capability/health, transition/error/cleanup, and pairing status without credentials. Raw-frame diagnostics are unavailable in B-2 even with consent.\n\nDo not send the whole Companion user-data directory. Review a diagnostic before sharing it and use the application-managed bundle.\n\n## Safe cleanup\n\nUse creator **Delete** for recordings. Stop the Companion before manual maintenance. Remove only generated validation `dist`, `.desktop-bundle`, or the resolved Electron `userData/companion` child after preserving desired recordings. Never delete a broad AppData or repository root.\n\r\n", "type": "input_text"}]

The original `main` checkout and completed B-1 worktree were not modified. The final source scope contains 70 added or modified files (56 source/configuration/test files and 14 development documents), grouped as follows:\n\n- 22 files under `apps/companion` for contract, core, target/worker, ring/quality, storage, pairing/loopback, coordinator, HWND/hotkey helper, and native tests;\n- Electron main/preload/command and packaged-smoke changes under `apps/desktop` and `scripts/desktop-smoke.mjs`;\n- shared TypeScript capture protocol, adapters, browser client, persistence service, UI, styles, APIs, feature flags, CSP, and service-worker safety changes;\n- additive Prisma schemas and one SQLite plus one MySQL migration;\n- application, desktop, Companion, security, persistence, and browser tests;\n- three ADRs and nine Phase B-2 engineering/completion records, plus two historical B-1 boundary annotations.\n\nPackage version is `0.4.0-b2`. `ws@8.21.1` is the only added production dependency. Existing development dependencies were moved to `electron@41.10.2`, `electron-builder@26.15.3`, and `concurrently@9.2.4`. `npm audit` and `npm audit --omit=dev` both report 0 advisories across 911 dependencies.\n\nMigrations:\n\n- `prisma/migrations/20260718090000_vision_capture_b2/migration.sql`\n- `prisma/mysql-migrations/0006_vision_capture_b2/migration.sql`\n\nGenerated, ignored release artifacts:\n\n| Artifact                                                 |       Bytes | SHA-256                                                            | Signature   |\n| -------------------------------------------------------- | ----------: | ------------------------------------------------------------------ | ----------- |\n| `dist/The Forever Treasure Companion Setup 0.4.0-b2.exe` | 243,160,218 | `838429920b404e324167d8bf1747909582787e588c522a21c62db221291ae367` | `NotSigned` |\n| `dist/win-unpacked/The Forever Treasure Companion.exe`   | 223,783,424 | `25057a9a2b23a315443351eafd04e76100f8b621604f024215d660cc9df02cbc` | `NotSigned` |\n\nElectron Builder produced the NSIS installer, blockmap, and unpacked application successfully. Production signing and updater hardening are explicitly reserved for B-6. Windows Application Control blocked execution of the final rebuilt unsigned hash (`spawn UNKNOWN` / application-policy block). An earlier package hash passed startup/listener capability smoke before the final desktop scan proof was added; the final source main process passed the stronger renderer-to-native scan, but the final unsigned package execution is not claimed as passed.\n\n## Final architecture\n\n```text\nShared /vision-companion UI\n  -> DesktopCapturePlatformAdapter -> context-isolated fixed IPC --+\n  -> WebCapturePlatformAdapter -> signed loopback WebSocket --------+-> CompanionCoordinator\n                                                                      -> one CaptureCore\n                                                                         -> window-only ElectronTargetProvider\n                                                                         -> sandboxed binary CaptureWorker\n                                                                         -> bounded ring + quality/selection\n                                                                         -> managed CreatorStorage\n                                                                         -> fixed Win32 HWND/hotkey helper\n```\n\nElectron main owns target enumeration, the coordinator, tray, exact sender/origin validation, and loopback service. The hidden sandboxed worker receives only an approved `window:HWND:other_id`, uses Chromium's supported selected-window `getUserMedia` path, sends 320x180 binary analysis buffers, and drains MediaRecorder WebM chunks. The renderer has no Node or filesystem access.\n\nPlayer scan defaults are five seconds at 10 FPS, configurable only within 3-8 seconds and 8-12 FPS. A frame/byte-bounded oldest-first ring holds at most 84 frames and 32 MiB. Temporal buckets plus perceptual diversity return 3-12 chronological metadata frame references. Consumption completes before pixel/luminance buffers are zero-filled.\n\nCreator media streams into a generated `.part` inside Electron's resolved per-user `userData/companion` root, with a 2 GiB file ceiling and 10-minute command ceiling. Finalization waits for late MediaRecorder chunks, calculates SHA-256, writes a strict sidecar, and atomically promotes the artifact. Cancel/error removes partial data; preview/delete accept generated IDs only.\n\nThe evidence bundle contains frame references, sequence/timing/dimensions, quality and motion summaries, capture/core/protocol versions, target privacy metadata, and an explicit cleanup receipt. It contains no pixels, path, location classification, or replay handle.\n\n## Architecture decisions\n\n- ADR 0011: Electron selected-window capture coordinator and sandboxed worker.\n- ADR 0012: loopback-only, exact-origin browser pairing using browser-owned ECDSA P-256 keys and signed challenges.\n- ADR 0013: fixed Windows `RegisterHotKey` plus selected-HWND health/release helper with no input synthesis or general key logging.\n\nNo governing discrepancy required an unapproved architectural reinterpretation. The capability is truthfully named `ELECTRON_DESKTOP_CAPTURER`; Chromium chooses the supported Windows backend and the application does not promise a fixed lower-level implementation.\n\n## Exact test Human physical-key/game/display actions remain in `B2_Test_Plan_and_Manual_Matrix.md` and are not silently marked passed.\n\n## Known limitations\n\n- Sea of Thieves borderless, normal-windowed, maximized, true-exclusive-fullscreen, multi-monitor, mixed-DPI, monitor-sleep, physical key release, visual preview, and gameplay frame-time observations were not available on this host.\n- Exclusive fullscreen is not guaranteed; frozen/unavailable capture gives structured guidance to restore or use Borderless Windowed. No injection fallback exists.\n- Windows 11 x64 is the implemented platform. Other Windows builds/hardware and non-Windows systems are not certified by this run.\n- Creator recording uses Chromium MediaRecorder WebM/VP9 where available. Capabilities report candidates and CPU metadata fallback; B-2 does not promise a dedicated hardware encoder.\n- The final unsigned package is blocked by this host's Application Control policy. Signing and production updater hardening remain B-6 work.\n- Raw-frame diagnostic retention is deliberately unavailable; an explicit include-frame request is rejected rather than silently retaining pixels.\n- A browser refresh discards its private key and therefore requires a new explicit pairing ceremony.\n- Creator database persistence requires an authenticated owner and draft waypoint; local media remains managed if that server write fails.\n- B-2 performs capture quality only. Recognition, geometry, reliability grading, story progression, Studio B-3 wizard, and Captain B-5 workflow remain deferred.\n\n## Phase B-2 exit gate\n\n### Architecture\n\n| Item                                                            | Status | Evidence / blocker                                                     |\n| --------------------------------------------------------------- | ------ | ---------------------------------------------------------------------- |\n| One native capture core serves desktop and browser-paired modes | PASS   | One `CaptureCore` in `CompanionCoordinator`; !== \"PLAYER_SCAN\") return;\r\n    await this.stopPlayerScan(this.active.sessionId).catch((error) => this.#fail(error));\r\n  }\r\n\r\n  async #handleHotkeyReleaseLost() {\r\n    if (this.active?.mode !== \"PLAYER_SCAN\") return;\r\n    this.active.interruptions.push({ code: \"HOTKEY_RELEASE_LOST\", at: new Date().toISOString() });\r\n    await this.stopPlayerScan(this.active.sessionId).catch((error) => this.#fail(error));\r\n  }\r\n\r\n  async #targetLost(code) {\r\n    const active = this.active;\r\n    clearTimeout(this.autoStopTimer);\r\n    this.autoStopTimer = null;\r\n    await this.worker.cancel(active.sessionId).catch(() => {});\r\n    if (active.mode === \"CREATOR_RECORDING\") {\r\n      await this.pendingWrites.catch(() => {});\r\n      this.pendingWrites = Promise.resolve();\r\n      await this.storage.cancelCreatorRecording(active.recordingId);\r\n    }\r\n    active.ring?.clear();\r\n    this.lastError = serializeCaptureError(captureError(code, code));\r\n    this.#move(\"TARGET_LOST\", { sessionId: active.sessionId, code });\r\n    this.active = null;\r\n    this.target = code === \"CAPTURE_SOURCE_CLOSED\" ? null : this.target;\r\n    this.emit(\"capture-error\", this.lastError);\r\n  }\r\n\r\n  async #fail(error) {\r\n    const normalized = error?.name === \"CaptureError\" ? error : captureError(\"INTERNAL_ERROR\", error?.message);\r\n    const active = this.active;\r\n    clearTimeout(this.autoStopTimer);\r\n    this.autoStopTimer = null;\r\n    if (active) {\r\n      await this.worker.cancel(active.sessionId).catch(() => {});\r\n      if (active.mode === \"CREATOR_RECORDING\") {\r\n        await this.pendingWrites.catch(() => {});\r\n        this.pendingWrites = Promise.resolve();\r\n        await this.storage.cancelCreatorRecording(active.recordingId).catch(() => {});\r\n      }\r\n      active.ring?.clear();\r\n    }\r\n    this.lastError = serializeCaptureError(normalized);\r\n    if (this.state !== \"FAILED\") {\r\n      try {\r\n        this.#move(\"FAILED\", { sessionId: active?.sessionId, code: this.lastError.code });\r\n      } catch {\r\n        this.state = \"FAILED\";\r\n      }\r\n    }\r\n    this.active = null;\r\n    this.emit(\"capture-error\", this.lastError);\r\n    this.#log(\"ERROR\", \"capture_failed\", { code: this.lastError.code, recoverable: this.lastError.recoverable });\r\n  }\r\n\r\n  #finishActive(response) {\r\n    if (this.active?.completionEmitted) return;\r\n    if (this.active) this.active.completionEmitted = true;\r\n    this.lastCompleted = {\r\n      sessionId: response.sessionId,\r\n      mode: this.active?.mode,\r\n      result: response.result,\r\n      completedAt: new Date().toISOString(),\r\n      selectedFrameCount: response.evidenceBundle?.selection?.selectedFrameCount ?? null,\r\n      artifactId: response.artifact?.artifactId ?? null,\r\n    };\r\n    this.lastCompletionResponse = response;\r\n    this.lastCompletionAt = Date.now();\r\n    this.active = null;\r\n    this.emit(\"capture-completed\", response);\r\n    this.#emitStatus();\r\n  }\r\n\r\n  #move(to, metadata = {}) {\r\n    const from = this.state;\r\n    if (from === to) return;\r\n    assertTransition(from, to);\r\n    this.state = to;\r\n    const transition = {\r\n      sequence: this.transitionHistory.length + 1,\r\n      from,\r\n      to,\r\n      at: new Date().toISOString(),\r\n      correlationId: this.active?.sessionId ?? metadata.sessionId ?? null,\r\n      metadata,\r\n    };\r\n    this.transitionHistory.push(transition);\r\n    if (this.transitionHistory.length > 500) this.transitionHistory.shift();\r\n    this.emit(\"state\", transition);\r\n    this.#log(\"INFO\", \"capture_state_transition\", { from, to, sessionId: transition.correlationId });\r\n    this.#emitStatus();\r\n  }\r\n\r\n  #health() {\r\n    if (this.privacyPaused) return { status: \"PAUSED\", reason: \"PRIVACY_PAUSE\" };\r\n    if (this.state === \"TARGET_LOST\") return { status: \"TARGET_LOST\", reason: this.lastError?.code ?? null };\r\n    if (this.lastError && this.state === \"FAILED\") return { status: \"ERROR\", reason: this.lastError.code };\r\n    if (!this.target) return { status: \"DEGRADED\", reason: \"CAPTURE_SOURCE_NOT_SELECTED\" };\r\n    if (this.state === \"PAUSED\") return { status: \"PAUSED\", reason: \"SESSION_PAUSED\" };\r\n    const frameAgeMs = this.active?.lastFrameAtMs ? Date.now() - this.active.lastFrameAtMs : null;\r\n    if (this.active && frameAgeMs !== null && frameAgeMs > 2_000) return { status: \"STREAM_FROZEN\", frameAgeMs };\r\n    const ring = this.active?.ring?.stats();\r\n    if (ring?.pressureRatio > 0.9)\r\n      return { status: \"DEGRADED\", reason: \"QUEUE_PRESSURE\", queuePressure: ring.pressureRatio };\r\n    return { status: \"HEALTHY\", frameAgeMs, queuePressure: ring?.pressureRatio ?? 0 };\r\n  }\r\n\r\n  #emitProgress() {\r\n    if (!this.active) return;\r\n    this.emit(\"capture-progress\", {\r\n      sessionId: this.active.sessionId,\r\n      state: this.state,\r\n      mode: this.active.mode,\r\n      progress: this.active.progress,\r\n      elapsedMs: Date.now() - this.active.startedAtMs,\r\n      frameCount: this.active.ring?.stats().frameCount ?? this.active.metrics?.length ?? 0,\r\n      droppedFrames: this.active.ring?.stats().droppedFrames ?? 0,\r\n      health: this.#health(),\r\n    });\r\n  }\r\n\r\n  #emitStatus() {\r\n    this.emit(\"status\", this.getStatus());\r\n  }\r\n\r\n  #log(level, event, fields) {\r\n    this.logger({ timestamp: new Date().toISOString(), level, event, ...fields });\r\n  }\r\n}\r\n\r\nmodule.exports = { CaptureCore, digest, randomId };\r\n", "type": "input_text"}]
